<Author>hea27
<Content>Restful and luxurious but not the best. Price: SGD399 + tax. Breakfast SGD44 per adult.Room: 13th floor, king bed, great size, spotlessly clean, superb bathroom (bath, shower, and two basins).Service: friendly and helpful. Location: across from the Marina/Esplanade. Linked by flight of stairs to Marina Square shopping centre. Less than 10 minutes walk to Raffles City shopping centre. SGD20 taxi fare from airport. Breakfast: delicious! Friendly staff and every possible thing you could want to eat. Expensive if you only want a quick bite. Pool  Spa: pool was very relaxing with a great view of the city. Spa was lovely but too expensive as you can get the same - if not better/longer - treatments at other top spas.Overall: a lovely hotel that we really enjoyed but won't re-visit. We splurge on luxury hotels when we don't have much time in the city, or when we really need a break and, unfortunately, this one didn't provide us with value for money. We thought breakfast was expensive, and internet access wasn't included either. If money is no object, then we guess you'll love it. But then again, you'll probably choose a better hotel!

<Author>Tsunami_5
<Content>Lovely views, Terrible service My husband and I were celebrating our wedding anniversary, so we decided to end our trip in the lap of luxury by staying at the Mandarin Oriental during our stop in Singapore.The hotel's exterior is unimpressive and not indicative of the modern interiors and stunning rooms. We were trying to decide between the Ritz Carlton and Mandarin Oriental (incidentally right next to each other with almost a shared courtyard), but chose the MO due to its floor-to-ceiling windows and high reviews.Overall, we were not as satisfied with the property as we'd like for the following reasons:- For the price charged and the kind of brand, service was extremely disappointing to say the least:1. God help you if you try to order a DVD...according to their in-room directory, you are supposed to call guest services if you would like to order a DVD after 11pm. When I called Guest Services, the lady was first surprised by my request and then transferred me to the concierge desk. No one answered the phone at the concierge desk, so I called guest services back and explained no one was answering the phone. Her response? 'Oh! Let me transfer you again' and before I could say anything, I'd been transferred again. Finally after a good amount of waiting, the concierge deigned to answer the call. When I tried to explain the situation and that I only wanted to rent a DVD, he cut me off in the middle of the explanation and said 'I will have a colleague bring up the list of DVDs to your room'. Of course, the colleague, much less the DVD menu, never showed up.2. I called Baggage Services to have our luggage picked up before 4pm as we were in a bit of hurry to catch our flight. The attendant asked for number of bags and confirmed someone would be at our door by 3:55. Of course, no one showed up. When I called at about 4:05pm, the attendant had no clue about the request and asked me for number of bags again and said someone would be up immediately...finally showed up at about 4:15pm.- Overpriced: the in-room dining rates are exorbitant for the kind of food. For 2 Penne Arrabiatta and 1 dessert, we were charged SGD 105. Though the pasta was nice, it was not worth the price. Dessert was great though.- Rigid: Breakfast stays open till 10:30, which is fine. If you happen to come at 10:28 like me and try to order omelette at 10:31, too bad. They will no longer serve from the buffet and you will have to order from the a la carte menu. As the staff is extremely busy cleaning up the buffet after the stroke of 10:30, service is extremely slow. At one point, it took the waiter 15 mins to get toast, by which time the rest of my husband's breakfast had gone cold.That said, the room was stunning with floor-to-ceiling window that faced the harbour and the Singapore Eye. Lit up at night, it was truly lovely.

<Author>BarneyGrimsby_UK
<Content>Won't go back Having stayed in Mandarin Oriental properties before, we were looking forward greatly to our stay.We arrived early in the morning after a very long flight from London expecting to check in straight away as we had paid extra for this, only to be told ourroom was not yet ready. Not a good start. They did provide us with coffee and toast from the breakfast buffet, but we had to sit in a corner almost in the corridor outside the breakfast room and were left to sit there for a couple of hours. Not good when you are exhausted and just want to get some sleep. A receptionist eventually came to find us only to tell us our room had been ready all along. No apology was given though. So we went to check in for the second time, only to find we were only booked in on a room only basis. Again we had paid for bed and breakfast. The receptionist was not pleased when I told her ths and dismissed this in an offhand way, eventually saying they would contact our tour operator. Too tired to follow this up further we went to our room.Our room was lovely. It was spacious and clean and had everything we needed. The bed was very comfortable and no noise could be heard from adjoining rooms or the corridor.There were several restaurants in the hotel but we only used the breakfat buffet. The other restaurants were expensive although they didi look nice. Singapore is full of excellent places to eat, why limit yourself to a hotel? The breakfast was excellent, with a huge choice. It only ever had about 3 people in it every time we went in. I'm not sure it warranted 4 staff at the door, each saying good morning and walking us to our table. Too much fuss for our liking. The fresh juice section of the buffet was particulalry brilliant with so much choice.The pool was good. The attendants rolled out the towels and brought fresh iced water regularly. We didn't spend much time here though. We had a view of the pool from our room and it never had more than a handful of people sat out there.The concierge seemed too interested in talking to his mate the first time we wanted to talk to him. The second time we tried, we asked about getting booked on the breakfast with the animals at th zoo. We were pleased to get this sorted. When we asked him to book us a taxi, we found we had been booked on an organised coach tour. It was very good, but this was not what we asked the concierge to do for us.Our problem with our booking was still not sorted the day before we were checking out. I had to get in touch with our travel agaent back home before this was acually corrected.The staff in the hotel are overly attentive. We felt uncomfortable with the fact that when you walked in the lobby there were at least 6 staff waiting to say good evening to you. I'm sure some people expect this sort of fawning, but it does nothing for us. 1 person is surely enough.The hotel has some very good points but we were not bowled over by the service we got. When we return to Singapore we will be looking for an alternative hotel.

<Author>DRKR
<Content>Avoid this hotel when travelling with kids! If you go to Singapore with kids, better avoid the MO! The hotel pretends to be child-friendly, so for a 4-days stopover way back from Bali to Europe we have chosen the MO (instead of the Shangri-La Valley Wing like last year): big mistake! As we wanted to have a drink before dinner in the Hotel-Lounge: no entry for kids after 5 pm is the strict rule; Club Lounge: no kids at all is the strict rule; Hotel Lobby: not existing. So there was no place for us for a relaxed champagne aperitif. Having asked the on-duty-manager for the sense of this regulation, the answer was Oh yes Sir, we are a child-friendly-hotel. Due to a prepaid room for my brother  wife next door to us we were unable to move to another hotel, so very unlikely we have sto stay here. Having a quite and not-runaway-kid and having stayed in a lot of luxury city-hotels, this was truly a unique experience: this did not happen in any othe hotel we stayed before. So if you have kids with you and like having aperitifs, you better avoid this hotel and stay elsewhere! The child-friendly-attribute is just pretending and not true.If you travel alone, the MO is OK, nice but very small (!) rooms (we had a Harbour Suite with beautiful view), and excellent breakfast (in Melt Caf茅); Dolce Vita Italian restaurant was nothing to write about , average food. But we were just glad, that we were allowed to go to the restaurants with our kid. Nice pool  well equipped fitness center. Service is excellent and on level of rating.

<Author>Floridot
<Content>Outstanding service, wonderful hotel I can't speak highly enough of our stay at the Mandarin Oriental, Singapore. From arrival to departure we receive the best service of the many hotels we stayed in on a round the world trip. We arrived very early morning after an overnight flight and were greeted with smiles and a lovely breakfast. We had a beautiful suite overlooking Marina Bay and the Singapore skyline and it was just perfect, with wonderful touches and the most comfy bed in the world. We ate in all of the restaurants and every one was a delight - particularly the Cherry Garden and Morton's. The swimming pool with regular service of iced fruits was just perfect after a hot day's shopping. We also made use of the Business Centre which had excellent facilities and the staff there were so helpful and courteous. The service as this hotel was outstanding, we felt that many hotels could benefit from the customer service training the Mandarin Oriental provides to its staff - they seemed to anticipate our needs before we even asked. The shops and attractions are really not far away and it was a delight to wander along the waterside, visit Clarke's Quay and see the Christmas lights on Orchard Road. This was a particularly special visit for my husband who lived in Singapore as a youngster so we looked forward to a very special return - we were not disappointed and we will certainly return to this hotel whenever we visit Singapore.

<Author>TonyLPerth
<Content>First class all the way The Mandarin Oriental rates as the best hotel I have ever stayed in. From the moment you enter reception you receive a very warm welcome that extends throughout the stay. We stayed on the 14th floor and the room was of reasonable size, but had a stunning view of the water. The bed was easily the most comfortable we have ever slept in, it was simply beautiful and enabled us to enjoy a very relaxing stay. The room decor was simple yet stylish, the bathroom functioned well and was luxurious, however doors to the toilet could be a useful addition.The buffet breakfast was extensive, fresh and offered a plethora of choice. The coffee/tea and table service was of the highest standard, however if there was one complaint I would make it would be that that the service at times was too efficient to the point where the coffee didn't taste as great due to all the top ups. The staff are very well drilled and there was only double up on a juice order which was amazing considering their workload.Over our stay the staff became friendlier (hard to believe but true) and the daily breakfast ritual become a pleasure. The dinner buffet was a feast, and was reasonably priced at $70 per person. Again as per the breakfast the choices were extensive.The location when taxis are cheap and plentiful was never a consideration. Singaporeans are very proud of having the F! come to them, and our room was directly opposite part of the track which did result in some daytime noise but nothing excessive. The hotel is adjacent to a well decked out shopping centre (set of stairs near hotel entrance) if you do not want to travel into the Orchard Rd district.A complete, luxurious and well appointed hotel worthy of a 5 star rating.

<Author>sambakongen
<Content>Nice but then it all came apart.... My wife and I stayed at the Mandarin Oriental for 6 days in late august following a 7 day stay at The Regent. We had booked a club room using the Mandarin Oriental promotion with American Express (stay 3 days and pay only for 2).We were quite pleased with the hotel until our 3rd day. Staying in a club room we had been to the club lounge each day for breakfast and although there was a sign at the entrance mentioning the dresscode (no shorts and no open-toed sandals) this was widely ignored by the guests and on the 3rd day my wife walked in in flip-flops and was stopped at the entrance being advised she could not enter in those flip-flops. Pointing our that from the entrance she could see 2 other ladies in similar flip-flops, she was advised that the other ladies were wearing flip-flops not made from rubber.... My wife went to the room to change and the following day the club lounge manager stopped me in my tracks asking if my wife was upset over the incidence? Why the club lounge manager did not ask my wife I don't know, but I said that my wife was of course upset at having been discriminated at. Then it all fell apart for the club lounge manager... She said that they had approached the other ladies in the club lounge after turning my wife away and asked them to change shoes as my wife had pointed out they were not following the dress code. Some lame excuses followed and the manager asked me if things were now in order since they had ensured no one showed up in flip-flops. I was flabbergasted!!! I tried to explain the manager that we had nothing against the other guests wearing flip-flops but we had something against the hotel choosing to apply its policies at the entrance to some people and not to others. As we stood in the entrance to the club lounge talking about this, 2 ladies by the way walked in in flip-flops and were not stopped. The club lounge manager had no clue what I was referring to - and that is the exact reason I will never stay at a mandarin oriental hotel again.

<Author>MorganJ
<Content>Just OK I stayed in the hotel for 2 days as a business traveller. My room was a Junior Seaview suite. My feelings with regard to this place is mixed. The location is alright but not really within walking distance to the cool shopping areas, and the coastal view is a bit gloomy. Its not really something for a holiday sort of stay. For business use, it was excellent location wise - very close to the financial district, yet still luxurious. Fairly quiet corner of the city.Optically, the building is pretty hideous (as is much of Singapore from this time period). Inside its obvious that it has been upgraded (a lot) inside - recently. The lobby, elevators and restaurants were definatly of 5 star grade. The front desk service and lobby staff, also. (classic asian style service, tons and tons of employees). The rooms themselves were not really to my liking. I mean, lets keep it real here - the room price of a suite - is under 500 euro - so compared to europe or attractive parts of the US, it's not exactly expensive. But... The bathrooms had dated style marble - which was not very nice, the ligthing was generally poor (which is never a good sign), the windows / sliding doors were of original vintage, which detracted from the luxury feel. The AC was sort of weird, if you put it on 20c, it was meatlocker cold, anything above 20c (incl. 20.5) equaled 35c++ and very high humidity. Weird. The carpet was nice, but never felt clean. The amenities were plentiful. The minibar and TV was very 1990's. Generally the room just didn't feel crisp in any way. Scrapes and stuff all over the place. The closets stank like they had been closed for 15 years. Also, the shower had nice long black hairs in it, not so nice. ;(Cleaning (besides from the hairs) was mediocre. So... I guess... Not horrible, not great. Personally, I wouldnt go there again.Oh, the Mortons steakhouse at the hotel was as good as the ones in the states. Very very nice.

<Author>Morpheus07
<Content>Impeccable Service We got an Executive Club room and requested a high floor. This was accommodated as we were on the 18th floor. When we got dropped off at the hotel, it was buzzing with people...at least 7 people were jostling into position to open car doors, check us in, welcome / greet us, open front hotel door, call the elevator, etc. I think over the 2.5 days there we were welcomed at least 100 times! The people are really warm and friendly and we can say was some of the best overall service that we have received. After a while it may seem a bit over the top but still nice! With the Executive Club room, you get access to the Executive Lounge on the 19th floor. Views are to the 'back' and not out the 'front' towards the marina or city skyline. That said, the food, snacks, drinks and comfort settings / furniture are very good. You can also use free wireless internet access up there...in case you don't know, the whole city of Singapore is wireless and anyone can register and access free internet, even tourists. I would also recommend paying the extra $20 or so to get a harbour / city skyline Executive Club Room looking over the 'front' rather than the 'back'. We made the mistake of not doing this.Pros- service, politeness of staff- quality of fittings and furnishings- cleanliness- foodCons- S$105 for a 1-way Merc E-Class ride to airport not worth the value (big S-Class Merc is S$155)- shopping mall attached to hotel is very average- Morton's Steak House not open for lunchOn a side note, we did the Night Safari at the Singapore Zoo and would recommend this for a good time.To wrap up, we'll be back!

<Content>Five star experience. We stayed five nights and six days and booked a harbour room through their Internet. We also booked airport pick up, used their concierge, exchanged money, checked out their gym, ate at their restaurant and used room service and dry cleaning/laundry. 1. Airport pick up: the driver was on time holding a paper printed with the guest's name outside the baggage area. We got the exact car that we wanted and it had two cold bottles of water and cold towels ready. 2. Check in: we were greeted right after we got out of the car and escorted to the room. Tea and fresh fruit was waiting. Our room was on the 20th floor with harborview. Luggage arrived quickly. 3. Room: floor to ceiling windows, extra amenities like emergency flashlight, umbrella, two robes, two slippers, complimentary bottled water daily, Molton brown toiletries, bath salts in tub, loofa scrub, some office supplies (staples, hilighter) room, night light. High tech lighting controls as well as privacy indicator. There was an indirect view from the bathroom due to the glass wall. Two toilet paper racks in bathroom, three phones (one in bathroom) a tub and a shower and one sink. 3. Concierge: excellent service and we used them to book a few tours (malacca was a good one but tiring, raffles tiffin, night safari riverboat, flyer). Money exchange was a breeze with them4. Dryclean: they found a button missing and insisted on paying for it. Price is high but expected. They returned our clothes the same day despite dropping it off at lunch. Laundry was neatly folded in a basket with a flower on top. Clothes were in plastic (not wires) hangers in the closet. 5. Room service: brought a table with food kept in a warmer. Arrived in 20 minutes and picked in five. Great selection of Indian,American local cuisine. 6. Location: across from the esplanade, attached to marina mall, walking distance to merlion, singapore river but we used cabs to go everywhere which was cheap. It was too hot to walk. 7. Food at The melt. Get the breakfast rate or it could be pretty pricey. We came in 10 min before closing and they extended the closing time. 8. Gym with cold towels water and techno equipment. Overlooking pool Spotless. 9.Customer service was their strongest asset. Always with a smile and anticipated our every need. No worries was their motto. Concierge walked you out after calling a cab. Housekeeping was excellent with attention to details. Change in throwpillows during turndown Amazing. Everyone knew our names. Minor quirks (which might just be me): wifi is not free,(30 sgd/day or 20/12 hrs 15/ 6 hrs etc ) it is free if you booked the club lounge. My pet peeve was that the hair dryer was attached. With that view I would have loved to move around. No flat screen tv but with surround speakers. Overall the best experience we've had in Singapore due to both the view and customer service We have tried the ritz and the four seasons (comparable customer service) but mo has both. We would definitely return. Suggest: try Singapore flyer, night safari, riverboat 30 min trip, malacca only if you have time, sentosa cable car, images museum, chili crab with man toux bread (east coast seafood).

<Author>Cooki
<Content>Spectacular Hotel with Unbeatable Service From the outside the Mandarin Oriental looks rather unimaginative, but as soon as you step inside you are transported to hotel nirvana. The lobby is spectacular, albeit somewhat dark, with striking artwork and a large reception area that easily accommodates large numbers of guests arriving simultaneously. We were greeted by lovely reception staff, and were upgraded to a suite and provided with late checkout til 6pm. Upon booking we had mentioned that we were traveling for our anniversary, so the hotel saw fit to put us up in a fantastic room. In less than ten minutes we were riding one of the panoramic lifts in the atrium up to our room.Although we have often stayed in hotel suites, this particular one was no mere hotel room, but rather a full apartment in itself, with a separate dining area, kitchen, living room, and bedroom. The decor throughout was impeccable, and the service continued to raise the bar. Perfectly timed with our arrival, our bags came split seconds later, followed by a complimentary fruit and tea tray. The bed was one of the most comfortable ones I have ever had the pleasure to sleep in, with a choice of pillows that satisfied even a fussy sleeper like myself.I feel that one of the hallmarks of truly great hotels is invisible service, and staff that can truly anticipate your needs. Housekeeping managed to slip in and out of our suite unnoticed, and the turn down service was perfectly timed to coincide with our dinner outings. The concierge was extremely helpful, and was able to provide suggestions that covered everything from entertainment to dining and shopping. The service throughout was simply outstanding - genuinely hospitable, knowledgeable, and efficient. The hotel is located a little bit on the periphery of the more happening spots, but taxis are fairly cheap, and are a widely used means of transportation. The MRT is also extremely efficient, but you will have to walk a bit to the nearest station, and Singapore is not very pedestrian friendly in all areas. As a result, we ended up hopping in a taxi every time we stepped out of the hotel.I would absolutely recommend this hotel to people who want to experience hotels as they should be - supremely comfortable, with friendly and efficient staff, immaculate service, and beautiful interiors.

<Author>tygerlily
<Content>Not 5 Star Customer Service; Not great for tourists As a sightseer this hotel leaves a lot for desiring. We found Singapore customer service in general was greatly lacking but we expected better at the Mandarin Oriental....and were disappointed. Customer service at the concierge/front desk was very spotty. We actually had a concierge tell us to walk several blocks out of our way to do a money exchange because he was too busy chatting with his female coworkers. Lobby not that impressive but rooms decorated nice enough. You can tell the bathrooms are a bit old but still nice. It's a fine hotel for business trips but not very romantic or leisurely. Good access to the malls by the harborside and once you get a hang of the thoroughways through the malls, you can access the subway (MRT) almost without going outside - although it's still a good 10 min walk. We took advantage of the food court directly across the street from the hotel which was nice. Expect to do a lot of walking if you're sightseeing Singapore and don't expect great customer service even at the nicer malls.

<Author>Kichi73
<Content>Loved the MO except.... As a local resident in Singapore, I decided to stay at the MO to watch the preview of the nation's National Day parade. As it was a busy weekend on Aug 2-3rd, the hotel was certainly put to the test in service standards. I was pretty perturbed when I reached the hotel for a check-in at 3pm and realised that my room was still not ready for occupation. I was told to wait for 1.5hrs. I was merely told I was to be allocated a higher floor than I had originally booked but not given any form of compensation while I waited. The front desk could have given me a welcome drink and told me to take a rest in the club lounge while I waited. Does that mean I had to wait and check time and again till I was eventually allocated a room? No answers were given. Was this the kind of service standards I had expected from a top ranking tripadvisor hotel? What's more, such service standards strayed from the usual standards I would expect from a MO hotel ! I began to wonder if It was because I was a local resident and not an international guest and therefore not given priority in room allocation. I know that front desk was under a lot of pressure but my point was that they could have been better prepared to deal with such a tight and pressing condition. I had no choice but to store my luggage with concierge and go ahead for a swim at the pool while I waited. Along the way, I was put through some inconvenience as I was still afterall a hotel guest, with no room but using hotel facilities. I waited patiently till half past five and still there was no news from front desk. I decided to go downstairs to front desk and after much difficuly, they finally found me a room. My question is - If I did not go downstairs at 6pm to enquire, would it mean that I was simply forgotten and had to wait till 7pm to get my room when I should have been given at 3pm? That would mean that I would have to miss half the show at the Marina bayfront where the preview was happning - the only reason why I chose to check in at the MO as it was directly facing the bayfront. I even had to remind the front desk there was a need for some form of compensation for the time lost. I was rather shocked such reminders had to be given after reading reviews about the excellent service standards at MO Singapore ! Are local guests not guests of the hotel at all? I was only able to speak to the Duty Manager subsequently who proceeded to apologise and compensate me for my time lost. The next day, I also received a personal apology note and a box of chocolates.Perhaps this was only an isolated event about their lack in service standards. The duty manager had superbly demonstrated the service standards of a top ranking hotel, so did the pool staff who remembered guests by name ( not all staff could do that ! ) as well as the some of frontline staff I met along the way. What I liked about the MO as compared to other hotels in Singapore is this - the huge buffet spread at MELT, the poolstaff who bend over backwards to provide excellent service and the awesome view of the harbour view rooms. Things to improve - service standards of front desk ,TV in rooms ( do consider changing to plasma or flat screen which the rest of the world is using ) and pl. treat all guests the same way, be it local or international. Although there was an unpleasant event I met during my stay, I still loved the MO Singapore, but do bear in mind that they should do better if they want to keep th top ranking on the tripadvisor website.

We realize that Singapore is more a business hotel type spot rather than a resort type location but with a few tweaks the MO could move into the heavenly zone occupied by the Shangri La chain and some others. <Author>skrosvik
<Content>The best hotel in Singapore MO is easily the best hotel in Singapore, after staying at RC and the Raffles. Whilst RC is cold and soulless, and Raffles are touristy and noisy - the MO is a warm and calm oasis and retreat. Check-in was very smooth, and got my room right away (at 11 am). The room was a superiour (I think it's the lowest category) on the 12th floor, it was newly refurbished and lavish, and very nice and comfortable. A bed to die for, and a large bathtub with seperate bathtub and shower. Large 42 LCD television with 80 or so international channels. Interactive telephone and also a cordless set, which was very convenient. The room had a large balcony overlooking Marina Mandarin. Not the best view, but it was nice to enjoy a cold cocktail in the sunshine.The staff and the service was great. The best service I have experienced in Singapore. Doorstaff and reception always greeted me by my lastname, and they were always smiling and very hospitable. The way MO should be:) The hotel does not have a grand lobby area, but they have a very nice bar on the 5th floor with a stunning view, overlooking Singapore harbour. There is also another bar, and 3-4 restaurants. Tried only the lounge and the bar - service, drinks and food were great. The breakfast (included in the room rate) was amazing, one of the best breakfasts I have ever had. There was a large selection of Asian and Western options, cold and warm, sweet and sour, light and heavy. You must try the breakfast when staying here. The juices are always fresh - made on request. Delicious.The hotel is located in Marina Centre - right next to the sea. I am not afraid of using my feet, so I walked everywhere without problem. The only times I used the subway was when going to Orchard Road and Chinatown. But you can easily walk to the harbour (just across the street) , the historic centre (10 minutes), Raffles (10 minutes), Singapore Flyer (5 minutes), Suntec City Mall (5 minutes), and so on... You can easily reach the subway if you walk through the mall that's connected to the hotel. All in all, the location is very convenient for sightseeing, business and shopping.If you love seafood you should visit Esplanade Mall across the street - there you'll find No Signboard Seafood. Strange name for a restaurant, but the food is absolutely delicious. It's quite inexpensive as well. Highly recommended!!I will return to the MO when going back to Singapore.

<Author>wasamaid
<Content>Top Class - as good as it gets My wife and I stayed at the Mandarin Oriental in July 2008, for only one night. En route from Darwin to Penang we decided to break our journey in Singapore. Upon our arrival at the hotel, we were overwhelmed by the efficiency and courtesy of the concierge and reception staff. We were then escorted to our room by a very pleasant reception clerk. We had booked a harbour view room (room 1403), and were very pleased with its appointments and features, and with its position. As a small feature, the hotel directory in our room was new and clean and not browsed by a hundred previous guests, as is often the case in other hotels. We had an uninterrupted view of the marina. However, as other trip advisors have noted, there is much construction work on two sides of the marina in this area of Singapore, and a floating stage is now positioned on the water, directly opposite the hotel. This detracts from the view, but there was no external noise. We arrived late, so chose to eat in our room. The room service menu was extensive, although expensive, but the food was very good. Breakfast at the Mandarin Oriental is as good as it gets, and is an experience in itself. Don't even think of having breakfast in your room. Staff remember the names of all guests, and the array of food is simply staggering, extending through several rooms. I seldom remember staff names, but one of our breakfast waiters (Ramees) provided us with exemplary service. Marina Square shopping centre adjoins the hotel. This hotel is quality through and through, and is as good as it gets.

<Author>PhileasFoggontour
<Content>Real Customer Service I've stayed at most of the big hotels in Singapore, and the reality is that there's a lot of positives about all of them. I had not, for one reason and another, stayed at the Oriental. As I continued to read reviews, and with the benefit of an Amex FHR made a reservation. My trip includes some other fine stops; the Ritz-Carlton in Singapore and then the Park Hyatt in Saigon. However, my expectation was that my stay at the Oriental was going to be the best of them all (and the other two were very good indeed).The stay was good, but it didn't reach the level that I was anticipating. Generally the hotel is superb, but there were some items and some issues that grated. One was relating to an airport pick up car that Amex had cancelled well in advance, that had turned up and been charged to my room and stayed there even at check-out. (I promise you Changi airport is the one airport in the world that doesn't need an airport limo pick up. The worst experience on your way into town will be the ever increasing Singapore traffic.)I got an online survey from the hotel after I had left and I took care to provide some feedback that I was less than overwhelmed with my stay. As I've said not a disaster, just some issues. I might even have said that I preferred the Ritz Carlton.I then got a message from the hotel asking if I'd be willing to discuss my feedback.So, in what would have been late at night in Singapore (I'm in New York) the most charming lady (Michelle) called me from the hotel and listened to my feedback, and issues and the charge that I'd never managed to remove. She even listened to my gripes about the cost of room service, and that the door man didn't know where the Ford Factory Museum was (not many people do, it's about the Japanese occupation of Singapore and well worth a visit for history buffs)And she said the right things, and had the charge fixed the very next day. Finally I got a pleasant follow up note from the Duty Manager (Mandy).So, I have to admit that the service in the end did win me over and I'll be happy to stay there again.My only word of warning about the hotel - and others nearby - is that there is a lot of construction in the area. A situation I suspect that is not going to improve between now and the F-1 race.

<Content>One of the best hotels This is truly one of the best hotels I've ever stayed in and it is mainly due to the excellent service. Everyone smiled and greeted us, often having a friendly chat. Just across the road from the hotel we stumbled on a night food market on the harbourfront which was very buzzy and had delicious inexpensive food. As we were on our way home from Europe, this was the perfect stopover hotel - luxurious, comfortable, everything we needed within walking distance so that we could just relax (and shop).

<Author>TravellersHobart
<Content>Wow what a place - service with a capital S We stayed only one night here before our return to Australia. We moved from the InterContinental because of the guaranteed 8pm check out in the Club rooms.We were offer an upgrade to a larger Club room - the only problem was it was a smoking room and we had requested a non-smoking room. The room had been de-smoked so there was no lingering smoke smell. The view over the harbour was spectacular. The room was spacious and the bathroom was beautifully designed.The decor of the Club lounge was inviting and the outlook was so good you could sit there with a very good cup of coffee or a very cold glass of champagne for a very long time. Staff in the lounge knew what service was and did it well. Nothing ever appeared to be a problem. They asked for the correct pronunciation of my surname so they could correctly address us. I travel under my maiden name (passport hassles) therefore my husband and I have different surnames on our hotel bookings but not once was I called Mrs husband name or my husband called Mr my name - they got it right everytime. The Club lounge had the most extensive breakfast menu of any of the Club lounges in the 3 hotels we stayed in Singapore this trip. With free flowing Moet champagne and the choice of items cooked to order for breakfast it was sensational. Evening cocktails were wonderful - basically anything you want and very good quality spirits used. Food at the evening cocktails was a hugh selection of tasty morsels.I just loved the place and would have liked to stay there for a lot longer - we will definately be back.

<Author>AreAnyNamesNotTaken
<Content>Superb I actually preferred this hotel to the vastly more expensive Ritz-Carlton next door, where I stayed on my last visit to Singapore. Of course, it can't match the RC for sheer sumptuousness, but it is cosier and feels as though a lot more effort went into the decoration and furnishings. Despite the Oriental's huge size, the tasteful rooms and well-equipped rooms manage to have a boutique feel that is unusual for this kind of business hotel.The public areas of the hotel are an extraordinary mish-mash of wacky architecture and clashing styles, from trendy modern Japanese to tacky 1970s European; whether or not this is to your taste is a matter of opinion, but it certainly makes a change from the usual faceless, identikit hotels that I spend so much of my time in. Unlike most business hotels, this is one that I would also be more than happy to book for a holiday (assuming I wanted to go to Sing on holiday!).

<Author>DonandHelen
<Content>DonandHelen My wife and I stayed at this hotel for 3 nights en route to Shanghai and 5 nights on the way home to Sydney. We have been to Singapore many times and have stayed at most major hotels represented. We always book for the Club floor (this is important) as it is a home away from home. <Content>Excellent A one night stay in March. They slightly messed up my arrival (at 0800 off an overnight flight) saying you cant check in til 2, but the supervisor sorted it pretty quickly, and gave me a complimentary breakfast while I waited an hour for my room.The room was good - about 200 square feet plus bathroom (separate shower, immaculate bathroom), and a balcony. The decor was fresh and modern while still high quality, the bed just right (not too soft or hard).At first I was a bit annoyed by the lift chimes, which were clearly audible in the rooms, but these are turned off at night so they didnt disturb my sleep.The lobby is quite dark wood, water and glass, distinctive in design but maybe a little heavy. The rooms sit on a series of inverted pyramid balconies, so each balcony looks dramatically down into a gulf - very striking.The staff are amazing - desparately keen to help. <Author>MrPJ
<Content>Perfection Stayed here for ten nights over Christmas whilst visiting family. Had a Club City Room, slightly larger than the Sea and Marina view rooms as I recall but not by much - a very good size. On every level I found it impossible to fault the hotel - staff were incredibly attentive and polite but never overbearing or appearing to be 'sucking up' or giving the impression you are a king. They just come across as genuinely happy to be at work and pleased to see you, like friends. We just felt totally at home throughout. I would almost everyone take a Club floor room. The Club offers excellent value for money and you can, if you wish, eat three meals a day up there (inclusive) incl. champagne breakfast and cocktails at tea. The Club staff are amazing and the whole Club experience made our stay extra special, providing the perfect place to relax and meet friends and family before venturing out. Choice of restaurants on site is exceptional and Melt totally changed out attitude to buffet. The quality of food was incredible so much so that after our first lunch visit we decided to have Christmas Dinner there too. Every festive food imaginable available including Lobster, monkish, sushi, roast turkey, brussel sprouts(!) indian, thai, chinese and, especially for the Antipodeans, an a open charcoal barbecue outside with a huge selection of meat and fish cooked on demand plus a whole lamb. it's not just quality though - nothing is on massive platters, just smaller plates, expertly prepared and replenished as required. Which made it easier to take small bites and enjoy a little of everything rather than stuff yourself on the first course. My mouth waters just thinking about it........ oh to be back there! Mortons Steakhouse on site is like being in the US - I've spent plenty of time in the US and it was like being teleported back there. Food, portions, service, style..... an incredible feat of theming and a fantastic meal. Then to working off the marvellous food......the gym is newly equipped and the well trained staff were, again, well beyond expectaions. The outside pool area was relaxing with great service from the staff. Concierge was spot on too - a little something I noticed was that the hotel staff gave all the taxi drivers a gift. Might have been Christmas or to highlight that it is now branded Mandarin Oriental and not just The Oriental. Which incidentally was the only problem, if any, during our stay. Despite the age of the hotel and its appearance in so many photos I could not believe the lengths we had to go to in explaining what hotel we were going to and where it was. Grasping Singlish helps but even then we needed to list every other hotel in the vicinity before drivers worked out where to go. But I think the gifts were a means to deal with this - a great idea. Totally recommended and I do not want to stay anywhere else next time. Perfect!

<Author>MrsM007
<Content>The Oriental - Sophisticated and Luxurious We've just returned from a trip to Singapore and stayed at the Mandarin Oriental. It was absolutely out of this world. On arrival, we were upgraded to a Club Room (I think that they are working on refurbishing some of the standard rooms at the moment, although the work being done wasn't at all disruptive). The room was quiet, very comfortable and extremely elegant. Being a Club Room, we had access to complimentary breakfast and evening cocktails in the Club Lounge, which were absolutely superb. We ate in one of the restaurants and had drinks in the bar - the prices are relatively high, but the surroundings and quality of service are both great. The gym is the best that I've seen in a hotel - well equipped and well staffed - and the spa is also lovely. All of the staff are polite and highly professional and the whole place has an atmosphere of understated sophistication, without seeming snobbish or overly formal. The only criticism that I had is that the pool area is situated quite near to a main road and although it's above street level, you can hear the traffic. All in all, an absolutely superb hotel.

<Author>mlb11
<Content>Still the best... I stayed at the MOH 2 years ago in a harbor view room right after they renovated. The room and facilities were first class. In early February, I stayed in a harbor view room again, now 2 years after the renovation and it is still first class. The rooms are very chic, comfortable, and the sound system very nice. The view is awesome! Read the other reviews concerning food and service - they are exactly right. If you do want to venture out and eat some good, cheap local food then go to the food republic located in the Suntec Convention center, about a 10 minute walk from the hotel (mostly indoors). I ate toast, eggs and kopi (coffee) there for breakfast on several mornings for under $3SGD. My only slight complaints with the MOH are the internet charge which is 50 cents a minute and soap/shampoo. Given the quality of services this hotel offers and the Mandarin Oriental Hotel group as a whole, they should not charge for the internet (especially in-room wireless). The soap/shampoo are okay, but seem a bit economical for the hotel. They should offer a higher quality brand of product such as my experience at other hotels that use Aveda, Thann, Juku, etc....

<Author>chrissievw
<Content>absolutely the best Having travelled extensively on both business and pleasure i can honestly say this is one of the best if not the best hotel i have ever stayed in. The location is great - walking distance from the city centre, raffles and all the major attractions. the rooms are big and beautiful, spotlessly clean and so are the pool and reception areas. The bars serve great cocktails and snacks. The breakfast buffet is without doubt the best i have encountered. yes it has all the usuals western style but all with a quality i have never come across before - fresh, plentiful and varied. But you can also choose from the japanese, chinese or indian buffets - mix and match. and it is all being cooked fresh in the open to view kitchen so its always piping hot. but such interesting and varied dishes. the bread staion has just everything and the fresh fruit covers a whole counter with tropical fruits i have never come across as well as all ones i am used to. they will even freshly squeeze a fruit smoothie for you from any combination. If possible the dinner buffet is even better - do NOT bother eating outside - we tried it one night and regretted it. The starters include huge prawns, oysters, crab and every kiond of meat and sushi as well as super fresh salad. Main courses are again set out on counters by nationality - the indian dishes are to die for or you can have your personally chosen ingredients stir fried with the most wonderful stock, or chinese or japanese as well as good all western joints, chicken etc. But the thing that puts this hotel above all others is the service. from the minute you walk through the door a myriad os staff are ALWAYS on hand to answer your every need - in fact they often ask to help even when you dont need anything. changing the duvet from my bed (too hot) into a sheet and blanket setup was done rapidly and without any reluctance. i was always greeted at the restaurant by name (how do they do that?) and escorted politely to a table. the bellboy even raced me to the lift to press the button. even the reception staff approached you with a smile as you neared rather than the usual frosty attitude as you try to get their attention. the pool attendant stopped what he was doing immediately to ask if i needed any help as i appeared in the pool area. i felt cosseted, cared for and cared about. i cannot praise this hotel enough. in singapore do not stay anywhere else.

Great atrium/foyer with the glass lifts whizzing you away to your floor, and there's always an attendant there to help with your gear.The proximity to Chinatown/Orchard Road/Transport facilities and even the Airport, make them all very handy and accessible.Very happy to lob here on future visits.

<Author>SydneyDan
<Content>Best hotel I've ever stayed in The Oriental Singapore was definitely the best hotel I've ever stayed in. I'm sure there are more luxurious ones somewhere in the world, but I've never stayed in them -- and I've stayed in quite a few five star hotels.Firstly, the interior of the hotel is just stunning. The entire centre of it is hollow, so you can look from the ground floor up to the very top. It's quite an amazing sight. Secondly, the buffet meals at the restaurant were just breathtaking. The spread goes on for rooms, with what must be easily over 100 dishes available at any one time. Every cuisine is catered for at all times of the day. The breakfast was particularly excellent -- the quality of every dish was a cut above what you typically get in a five star hotel.The staff were impeccably attentive and polite. From the moment we were picked up at the airport by limo and then greeted at the hotel with extremely fast checkin (everything done in advance for us) to the many, many staff available all around the hotel to help you.The hotel gym and spa was very nice, with attentive gym instructors and free bottled water, towels and headphones. The selection of restaurants in the hotel was amazing -- apart from the main buffet restaurant, there were many other bars and restaurants, and even one standing alone from the hotel near the spa. All in all, the Oriental experience made my business trip vastly more enjoyable and I have been hankering to go back for a holiday ever since!!!!

<Author>Davidob
<Content>Marvellous Mandarin I stayed at the Mandarin for three nights in a Club Harbour View Room as part of a month鈥檚 trip around Singapore, Malaysia and Thailand. Check in at the hotel was very quick, efficient and friendly and we were soon escorted to our room on the 19th Floor. The view of Singapore was marvellous and the room was very well equipped, with very comfortable bed, flat screen TV and cabling to enable MP3s etc to be connected to the sound system. The room was not particularly large but was beautifully furnished with an equally well furnished bathroom complete with separate bath and shower and plenty of nice Molton Brown products. Staff and service at the hotel couldn鈥檛 be faulted with the perfect mix of very friendly but unobtrusive service with staff anticipating your every needs. The Club Lounge was a great bonus with excellent breakfast and snacks and cocktails, loved the seared tuna and the excellent lamb chops! Also had breakfast in Melt but much preferred to have it in the Club Lounge with the freshly cooked options. One little niggle was the limit of 15 minutes free internet access in the club lounge even when the lounge was empty, free wifi was also available if you had your own laptop.All in all a very enjoyable and faultless stay and I would definitely recommend upgrading to club lounge access.

<Author>munthe
<Content>couldn't fault it! We recently spent christmas at the mandarin oriental, we stayed for 1 week in total and thoroughly enjoyed our stay. The breakfast was a huge spread and everything was fresh and delicious. The overall service given by all staff in the hotel was excellent. However what I would say is that if you are used to staying in 5 star hotels in asia then the service is exactly what you would expect in hotels of that standard. Some of the previous reviewers seem to go over the top about the service and so can appear misleading. I suppose it's what your used to and admittedly the service in hotels in europe nowhere near compares.The location is great if you want to be near the quay area and also convenient for shopping. The marina square mall adjoins the hotel and you can cross through there to the suntec city mall so everything is close by. Its only a short, reasonably priced taxi ride to orchard road and there is also the mrt close by. One thing I must point out if anyone is wanting a good family dinner on christmas eve then this is the place to be. We were 4 adults and 3 children and we spent a very pleasant evening in the melt world cafe. The children were well catered for with their own room with toys, cartoons and 4 members of staff watching them. They had there own candy floss machine and as much to eat as they wanted, this gave us adults a nice relaxing evening too.

<Author>zabo
<Content>Great Location I had a 4 night stay at Oriental Singapore whilst attending a large medical conference. at the end of July 2007.The hotel is located in the heart of business district of Singapore on the marina and close to many 5 star hotelssuch as the Pan Pacific, Meritus Mandarin, Ritz Carlton, shopping malls and directly connected to the large Suntec Convention centre where the conference took place. A good thing about this part of town is that most malls are linked and there is a large underground mall pass connecting you to the famous Raffles area and the metro..I travelled alone and had a deluxe sea view room overlooking the harbour and part of the marina. The room was clean , comfortable and spacious enough for a couple. A plus in the room was a DVD player and Ipod port .Furnishing was modern with an oriental touch.The bathroom was luxurious with a separate shower and generous bathtub and ample amenities..Breakfast was included in my rate and very good with quite a selection including indian. south asian and american treats. The surrounding skyline at night was amazing to behold and I particularly enjoyed strolling along the waterfront at night which was very safe.Although this hotel is about 15 mins from the famous shopping Orchard Road, the surrounding malls do have lots to offer and as this was a business trip I found the location very convenient.I would recommend this hotel for business travel or short stopover in Singapore

<Author>hagsdownunder
<Content>Good position otherwise average Yet again our booking was mixed up but unlike the Shangri-la the front desk manager (!) made us wait- (there was nowhere to sit- as the few chairs available were occupied) while she attempted to rectify their mistake. We then (after a long flight) had to wait around until 3.00 pm. before our room was available. This is a hotel for business people; its position overlooking the marina is great but there is none of thepersonability of the staff or of the hotel. The decor is ... minimalist or just not fitted out. There are three large reception rooms in the entrance which could have some chairs for guests waiting when not used for conferences! The Melt restaurant offeres a very comprehensive buffet which could feed half of Biafra but is pricey in their a la carte. (I am also so tired of waiters whipping plates away before you have finished chewing!)The rooms are very pleasant- decor good, beds comfy and good pillows. The entertainment system offers many music channels which we love and seem to be offered less and less in Asian hotels.The pool is hopelessly lacking in loungers- we watched many guests being turned away because they had no-where to lie. However the attendants were great- giving us regular bottles of water and little sweet treats from the kitchen.There are many shopping opportunities close by and the MRT is a 5 min walk away. Internet access is as usual expensive at S$30 per day.

<Author>Aussieholiday
<Content>Loved the Mandarin Oriental, Singapore I am writing to inform you all of the wonders of the Mandarin Oriental hotel in Singapore. We found the experience to be one of sheer luxury. I would urge anyone contemplating a stay in Singapore to seriously consider this option out of the many, many available to choose from. In terms of value for money ...it was a hit. We booked early and directly with the hotel and secured a great rate of around $300 AUD per night for 2 adults and 1 child with breakfast included. Fantastic, given the excellent standard and quality of the hotel. As a bonus, the roll out bed was free of extra charge; a rarity for the other Singapore hotels that I had checked out. My husband has worked in a global role out of London but based in Sydney for the last 10 years. As a consequence of this, he has spent much of that time travelling the world. I have been very fortunate to be able to join him on many trips and have experienced many 5 ~ 6 star hotels. I would have to say that the Mandarin Oriental ranks most highly. We found the attention to detail across all aspects of service provision to be excellent. The most notable point was the friendly and courteous attitude of all staff; from the staff who handled my initial e-mail enquiries to the Concierge and dining staff and right down to the pool and gym staff. They all expressed good cheer and humour and genuinely appeared to love their work and to be committed to making the hotel function at optimum performance. We were also greatly impressed by the size of our room (we were upgraded to a Junior Suite), the quality of inclusions and the care taken to clean the room, attend to 'turn down' of an evening and to replenish bathroom items. The latter point may seem a minor one but, can lead to irritation if unattended! Similarly we were very impressed with fit out of the gym, the hotel landscaping, the pool and its surroundings. I walked over to check out the Fullerton which, in my opinion, pales in comparison to this hotel. In terms of children, this would definitely be your choice of hotel in Singapore as: the pool was huge and surrounding area was great, you are away from the intense hustle of Orchard Rd, there are great cheap-eating Hawker food markets across the road and beautiful, riverside plu other walks in all directions from the hotel. There is a greater sense of space in and around this hotel compared the Fullerton and Orchard Rd hotels that would appeal to anyone with kids. Anyway, taxis are so cheap that all venues are easily and cheaply accessible. I have already recommended your hotel to my friends who travel and our friends based in Singapore who we were visiting. The Mandarin Oriental would be a definite choice for our preferred accommodation if we ever to choose to stay in Singapore again!

<Content>Luxury We stayed in a club room on the 20th Floor for 5 nights. The room was big with a fantastic bathroom where you can look straight out to sea from! However it only cost around 拢1 for a taxi to Clarke Quay and about 拢2 to Orchard Rd. We did walk to Clarke Quay which only took around 15 minutes! I do agree this hotel is more of a business hotel but it's still worth staying there for a little bit of luxury.

<Author>SydneyKeen_Traveller
<Content>Better service than the old Oriental Stayed here again for 4 nights on business in a deluxe harbour room. Last stayed at the Oriental in early 2007 before the change in name from the Oriental to the Mandarin Oriental. Was truly but pleasantly surprised at the enhanced level of service in the hotel - more friendly, obliging, thinking ahead staff then the former Oriental. As a regular traveller to Singapore (for business and leisure) have found in the past that, in most hotels here, staff can be friendly but have robotic smiles and there is always an element of arrogance in the service level - quite a big difference to the servicelevels in the hotel industry in Thailand. Maybe it was the rebadging of the hotel's name or maybe it has to do with the recent Singaporean government's attempts to unshackle some of its control over the citizens and encourage creativity and fun in this city state. But whatever the reason is the result is most welcome.As this is a business trip paid by my employer, did not check-in into a club room and hence did not have access to the club lounge and otherclub facilities (which I have previously experienced). But the deluxe room was fine - no Molton Brown toiletries and access to the Cub lounge with free internet or food and beverage, and still a CRT TV butotherwise still a luxurious and comfortable room to stay in. But the pleasant surprise this time is that my room rate includes the daily breakfast at Melt which is really outstanding. The buffet spread is even better and more varied than my best to date (Peninsula Bangkok). One has a choice of having an English, American, Continental, Chinese,Indian, Korean, Japanese or Malay breakfast (and can of course mix and match) on a daily basis. One can easily skip lunch after such a big and elaborate breakfast. Breakfast in the Club Lounge, however, is a more sedate continental affair.Agree with most of the positives said about this hotel - which I won'trepeat, however, a few pointers to would be residents:- if possible and affordable stay in a club room- view from a harbour room is better from the ocean room or city view rooms (the latter generally means you will get a view over Suntec Cityor Marina Square, which is not very interesting)- the hotel obviously has either not completely refurbished all the rooms or has decided to leave some rooms more traditionally furnished and equipped (and not like the rooms one can see on the website). To avoid this problem always ask for a room with an MP3 dock(even though you may or may not want to carry one) which means that you will a more up to date room, with DVD player, MP3/ Ipod and video camera docks, surround speakers / sound system and better bathroms (but without a bidet which was available in the other room type). - if booking a non Club room, try to get a rate which includes breakfast. At around SGD$40 (incl. tax) per room breakfast is not cheap by Singaporean hotel standard but is definitely worth it on an all inclusive room package.- If you are staying in a Club room you have access to 8.00pm late check (and you do not have to be an AMEX centurion card member) - this is confirmed in the hotel directory available in all rooms and on the hotel's website. This is ideal for travellers with night flights to Europe or Australia.- From a location perspective, the hotel is next to a massive shoppingmall (historically has been preferred by the locals from value for money perspective; however if you are shopping for labels go to megastores and shopping complexes in Orchard Road which tend to be more catered for overseas visitors). There is no direct link from the hotel to the shopping mall (it was blocked for security reasons in the last refurbishment). But one only has to walk outside, turn right,climb up the stairs and voila. This huge and meandering shopping mall is connected to City Hall MRT station (approx. 10 min walk) and is fully air conditioned. It is only near the MRT Station that one is temporarily exposed to some hot and humid spaces.- local taxis are really cheap by international standard for both business people and tourists. One can get around the central parts of the City (incl. Chinatown, Raffles Place and Orchard) for between SGD5to SGD10 (unless one is unlucky enough to be stuck in traffic). Sure, trips on the MRT are much cheaper (e.g. City Hall to Orchard Road is SGD0.90 per trip! but my recommendation is if time and energy are limited grab a taxi. But avoid the limo taxis (unless desperate) as these will normally charge you SGD20 even for a short trip. If you aretravelling from Orchard Road back to the hotel, be patient, as you will have to queue for a cab (some queues can take 30 to 40 mins). But there are shorter queues at the neighbourhood hotels or side streets (the side queue at the Paragon is a good find on this trip). Otherwise take the MRT to City Hall and walk back to the hotel.One negative and unfortunate thing that I noticed in my last 2 trips to Singapore this year is that hotel prices in Singapore have increased. My local contacts tell me that this is due to an increase in tourism into Singapore, more conventions and exhibitions and special events happening in Singapore (e.g. a Grand Prix for the firsttime next year) and hardly any new hotels being built (most have been refurbished) for quite a few years. The new hotels in the integrated resorts being currently built in Marina Bay and Sentosa will not be finished until until say around 2010.So don't expect the 5 star bargains that one can previously have in Singapore or can still have in KL or Bangkok. But if you are planning to be here, the Mandarin Oriental is great place to stay in.  
<Date>Nov 10, 2007

<Author>NicC
<Content>Nice hotel but location not so great The Mandarin is a great hotel but the location does let it down. Whilst for business guests I guess this is not so much of a problem, but for tourists who have a few days, I would not recommend this place so much unless they got to grips pretty quickly with the transport options.Hotel itself, cannot fault. We didn't get any Molton Brown toiletries that I read of in one review - maybe this is just for Club guests? Incidentally the hotel tried very hard to flog this option to us - it just didn't seem to make economic sense. The breakfast was wonderful but we found the restaurant prices obscenely expensive. Made the mistake of eating at Mortons one night (we'd left it very late to eat, our feet hurt too much to go out and it was the only place that would take us at 1030pm at night in the hotel) and I was shocked by the rip-off prices. S$ 20 for a Martini, when you can get a fabulous one with views to boot at New Asia Bar at the Swisshotel for S$12? S$35 for one tiny crab cake? I refused on principle to order a main course as I felt that to charge those sort of prices for something that would cost a quarter of the price outside was taking the michael. Service was annoyingly American, with waiters wanting to 'present' the menu to us instead of just letting us read the menu! Next thing they will be giving a slideshow. Plus they never let us alone for a minute. Not the place for a romantic dinner.The concierge was not well informed on bus routes - I guess he is more used to helping business guests and hailing cabs. We wanted a bus to the Orchid Gardens and was told that there was only 1 bus that didn't quite go as far - not true. Luckily the bus driver helped out and put us right. There's a bus that takes you right there BTW.This leads me to the location. Not great for tourists. Whilst you can walk, in the sapping heat that's not always an option. City Hall MTR is about 10 mins away and not much use if you want to go to Chinatown or the Quays as this involves a nightmare change at Doby Ghaut. My recommendation is to go across the road and get a bus from Esplanade Mall. The bus maps are easy to work out, they are cheap, and air conditioned! First 2 days we used taxi, then graduated to MTR, but finally worked out the buses were the best way to go. There are loads of buses that go direct to Orchard Road.Next time we visit Singapore, we'd choose the Fullerton. Great hotel in a very central location.Don't bother going to Raffles for the Singapore Sling - what a disappointment and waste of money! DO visit the Swisshotel on Stamford Road and head to New Asia Bar for great cocktails at sunset. We enjoyed Clarke Quay area very much at night, and had the most wonderful brunch at Marmalade Pantry in the Palace Renaissance mall on Orchard Road. Shops don't open until around 1030/11am, so it's great to go there for a late breakfast before the shops open.  
<Date>Nov 7, 2007

<Author>lieblingsg
<Content>Best Hotel in Singapore I have stayed at many top end hotels in Singapore but I think I have just discovered one of the best that Singapore has to offer. I am referring to the new revamped The Mandarin Oriental Singapore, formerly known as The Oriental. I used to be a member of the gym at the hotel many years ago and I had stayed in their rooms during those period. I would not wax lyrical about my experiences then.The hotel was part of the Marina Square development near the city centre and was part of a trio of hotels, namely, Marina Mandarin, Pan Pacific and The Oriental. The Oriental as it then was had always been the best of the three though. Its neighbour, The Ritz Carlton Millenia, came into the scene as the first 6star hotel In Singapore and had always somewhat overshadowed The Oriental. However, since this hotel became part of the Mandarin Oriental fold, it has metamorphosed into the most luxurious hotel in town. I have stayed in the hotel twice, once over the August 2007 National Day holiday and the other last weekend. My first stay was in a huge corner suite with a south view and that of its neighbour, The Ritz Carlton. The second stay was in a normal deluxe room with a West facing view of the city skyline. On both occasions, I had access to the Club Lounge, which is the reason why a stay in this hotel is very highly recommended.The Club Lounge is the most luxurious facility of its kind in any hotel in Singapore. I have been to a few of these in other hotels but the one in Mandarin Oriental is by far the most luxurious, beautiful and inviting. The d茅cor is something out of Elle D茅cor Magazine with 2 types of seating, plush sofas or small dining tables. The walls are clad in pleasing exotic dark wood veneer and tribal artifacts tastefully adorn the lounge area. The Club Lounge is bathed in natural light which comes in from a high floor to ceiling window panels. There is a library near the reception area but coffee table books are placed everywhere for your reading pleasure. If you have access to the lounge during your stay, this is where you can have breakfast away from the madding crowd, indulge in high tea or enjoy evening cocktails. Between 5.30pm to 7.30pm, that is the best time to hang out at the Club Lounge. That is when they serve gourmet food! Last weekend, they had North Indian food on one evening and French on the other (foie gras maison and slices of magret de canard a l鈥檕range anyone?). During my previous stay, the food was Thai. The food is simply delicious and enough for you to skip dinner altogether. But that means forgoing a delightful selection of superb restaurants in the hotel, including Mortons for exceptional steak.If you don鈥檛 have access to the Club Lounge, there is a coffee lounge on the 4th floor with a harbour view and plush setting. And if you don鈥檛 eat out, order room service. Even its room service food is top notched and the food comes with such beautiful presentation. My order of seafood chowder was absolutely delicious and came chock a block with a treasure trove of shrimps, mussels and scallop. My order of Tom Yam Goong was served in a petite young coconut. In other words, this hotel has the Mandarin Oriental quality stamp all over. This also applies to the service for which Mandarin Oriental is famous for. From the bellboys, to the reception and down to the chambermaids, everyone greets you with a smile. As you check in, a personel will escort you to your room or to the Club Lounge. The service is both assured and confident. You cannot say the same about this in many other establishments on the island.The rooms are very tastefully done with a lot of wood and marble in the d茅cor. The beds are very comfortable and the bathroom adequately spacious with a separate bathtub and shower areas. The toiletries from Molton Brown are quite exotic and very refreshing. Whilst the rooms are not equipped with a plasma TV, the touch screen universal remote for the TV makes navigation for in-room entertainment a breeze. I recommend a room with the harbour/city skyline view. It will take your breath away despite the sight of towering cranes all over the construction site for the integrated resort. The sunset and water view is worth the extra penny. They also pamper you with a generous fruit bowl, a delicious cheese platter plus a bottle of wine.I did not try the spa, so I cannot comment on that. The fitness centre has been upgraded and is now 10 times better than what it used to be. The fitness centre is no longer open to public membership which explains its quality. The hotel pool is definitely one of the best here as it offers you a good depth and length enough for you to do short laps.If you are an Amex Centurion Card holder like me, you have extended check out until 6pm, which gives you all the extra time to indulge in the luxury that this superb property has to offer. I would recommend this hotel highly for a superb weekend getaway even to Singaporeans. My experience here is 10 times better than that in Mandarin Oriental Kuala Lumpur (see separate review).

<Author>bluechick
<Content>Pure luxury I stayed at this hotel in August 2007 after a trip through Malaysia. Having stayed in cheap hotels through Malaysia I wanted to book luxury for the last stop. And I'm glad I did! I got a stay 4 nights pay 3 deal which made it much cheaper. The room was lovely and the bathroom was beautiful. The breakfast was also amazing. Great location as well, and ocean views. I also enjoyed the pool with its city views. Being unused to staying in these kinds of hotels however I did feel there were a couple of downsides. Another reviewer mentioned the overservice and I felt the same. It felt like I couldn't turn a corner without someone there to open a door for me and it made me feel more like I was constantly being watched. But the shop assistants do that as well in Malaysia/Singapore so I think it is just their way. Other complaints were the price of everything - use of internet in the business centre was hideously expensive (there is a very cheap internet cafe up the road) - and also having only duvets on the beds in a city that is constantly hot and humid meant for a couple of very warm nights. To be fair though, I never asked for the bed to be changed so that might have been available if requested.Overall, thoroughly enjoyed my stay and would definitely recommend it. Singapore is also a lovely city and so safe for a solo female traveller!

<Author>RNBNY
<Content>They converted me I have to say, after many years of the Raffles and the one time they were fully booked, I had to try the Oriental. It sounds like a complaint, but far from it. For a modern hotel, this is truly luxurious. I do agree that the in room check-in is irritating, but I have to stay it was nice being whisked up to the room after a long trans-pacific flight. The lobby space is impressive though not beautiful, but the views from the room overlooking the harbour are stunning. It is a little out of the way, but taxis are available. The staff is very professional and extremely gracious. The bath is delicious, and room, though slightly small still wonderfully appointed. The lounge is a lovely space and pool pleasant. Staff suggestions are surprisingly good, unlike most that guide you to overly touristy places. The best part was a fantastic bowl of congee at 5:00 a.m. just before departure. There is an art to making it, and the service was superb. This is my new home in Singapore, and would suggest anyone to give it a try. There is something to the Raffles, but the Oriental surpasses in every way.

<Author>hanyu
<Content>Renamed and revamped. A lot of improvement. I'm a fan. Stayed at the renamed Mandarin Oriental Singapore over a weekend when in town to see some relatives as a stopover on the way back home. I've stayed here before some 6 years back and been to the Shangri-La, Fullerton, Four Seasons and Ritz-Carlton. I was curious about the heavy advertising on the renamed, rejuvenated spiel for this branch of the Mandarin Oriental chain and opted to stay here. I got a harbourview room.Incentives:1) There has indeed been a marked improvement in the hotel since several years ago. I was honestly impressed with the change. The hotel looks refreshed and even though the building itself isn't that new, the hotel and its facilities/furnishings have all been upgraded and/or well-maintained.2) With the new casino coming up and move of the business/downtown area to the bay area, The MOSG is in an excellent location for business in the future along with already lovely views pegged to improve as 2010 looms. 3) It is next to a major mall with food and shops readily available though it is not directly connected to it like the Pan Pacific. This means having to walk outdoors and risking some rain frequently but I personally didn't find the 2 minute journey that much of a hassle.The local theatre and concert hall is right across the street for those with artistic intents.4) The service is truly top-notch and in this reviewer's opinion, now the best in town. The staff were all sincerely friendly and smiling with greetings that didn't sound too artificial or over the top like in some places. They opened lift doors and the doormen were always ready to assist. Memorably, housekeeping polished 2 pairs of shoes for me and even declined a tip saying it was a pleasure to be of service and he enjoyed polishing really good quality shoes! In all my years of travel, I've never encountered such a thing and am truly impressed. This attention to personal detail and individual touches by the staff helps make one feel special and at home and differentiates the truly international world-class from mere 5 stars.They have clearly exceeded anything Fullerton, Ritz-Carlton and Four Seasons have provided in the service department. Only the Shangri-La compares but the Shang's location isn't as convenient for future business come 2010 and truth be told, it is also getting a little long in the tooth.5) They have a great collection of restaurants and breakfast was excellent. Morton's, the chinese restaurant and the cafe were all consistently good places. This is useful for business trips since meal meetings can be right at the hotel without sacrificing food quality.Discentives:1) The only blimp on service was that I checked in with a request for a non-smoking harbourview room , which was accepted when I made a booking, only to be sent to a smoking one. When I called front desk, the person on actually told me they didn't have anymore non-smoking rooms. This is clearly wrong and my booking shouldn't have been accepted to begin with or I should have been told at the front desk rather than after I came up to the room. To the hotel's credit, the front desk manager immediately took charge when I expressed unhappiness and moved me into a better non-smoking room with a better view and sent up bellhops to move my luggage. These personnel also declined any further tip as part of the apology for the error. She also called to personally apologise for the mistake.2) The rooms are functional at best with little character or space. However, closet and storage space is quite excellent.One can argue that prices for rooms in Singapore are very reasonable next to Hongkong or even Bangkok for the upper end but a little more space would be nice. The next door Ritz-Carlton fairs better in this department.The lack of character and amenities seems to be a Singapore hotel thing in general. Even the lauded Fullerton's Philippe Starck room furnishings were somewhat perfunctory overall in design when put together though each individual piece was often quite avant garde.The special extras found in MO NYC and HK were all missing like decked out multi-fax phones and flat screen TVs in the bathrooms.3) The hotel rooms still use cathode-ray tube TVs. This is already quite unacceptable for 5 star world city standards. However, the facility to iPod link to the the room sound system is pretty good. 4) The need to exit the hotel in the open to get to the nearby mall has already been mentioned.5) No underground mass transit service is nearby and public transport ex-taxis are not a feature of this hotel or the nearby Ritz-Carlton.6) For a revamp, it is disconcerting to see they still use the old name The Oriental on the clothes hangers, writing instruments and toiletries while the mineral water and paper etc. trumpet Mandarin Oriental. This is somewhat inconsistent, though to be fair a more minor point.Taken in total, the MOSG has indeed impressed me and seems to be a true member of the aggressively expanding MO chain. While minor points remain that peg it lower than its compatriots in Tokyo, Hong Kong and Bangkok, this is true of all Singapore hotels in general.When in Singapore, weighing all the hotel options, I would definitely opt to stay at the MOSG again. It is my pick for a Singapore hotel. I'm a fan.  
<Date>Oct 9, 2007
