<Author>Peelay
<Content>Just average We had just stayed at the Mandarin Oriental in Hong Kong a month before, and given it's cut from the same cloth and had allegedly just been renovated too, staying at the Oriental in Singapore you would not have known they were related. Pet hate - in room check in which they are quite insistent on and had to be firmly dissuaded from trying again, after our first experience of it. Took forever, no need. Why do they insist on coming into your room with their shoes on?The room finishings were cheap and the touch screen remote control for the tv, just annoying, as were the ceiling speakers. Big hole in the ceiling above the shower that was just not filled in. Cheap slatted blind to hide the glass wall separating the bedroom area and bathroom - why bother with a glass wall at all if you're not going to put the bath there as a feature. Bad, bad design. Cheap products in the bathrooms.Huge and impressive atrium space but most of the rooms are linked to outside corridors around it and therefore noisy. Request a room at the end of these corridors. Communal corridors featured ripped and dirty wall papers. Has it been totally or partially renovated?A ridiculous number of staff to meet and greet all of whom want to take your bag and ask you the same question. Very tiresome indeed. Good choice of restaurants, from Mortons to the Melt the World Cafe (Melt - The World Cafe actually, but we preferred the former way of reference). MtWC seems to do the buffet thing at all times. Disappointing; wouldn't stay there again.

<Author>laleitz
<Content>Indulgent and Relaxing stay at the Mandarin I met my husband for a stay in a City View, Club Level Room at the Oriental, and it was absolutely the right place for us to stay. The whole hotel environment is one that feels utterly serene and indulgent. The room was well appointed and I appreciated the little touches the housekeeping services added each day.The hotel is located an easy 10 minute walk to the City Hall subway station, and it is possible to do almost the whole walk indoors through various malls if Singapore is having one of its torrential downpours.. Getting cabs was super convenient, and the workers hailing the cabs were so nice and actually funny!The Club perks were worth every penny- free internet in the lounge, extra help with concierge services, champagne breakfast, non-alc drinks all day, and evening cocktail and hors d'oeuvre hour. The breakfast was a nice blend of waitress service and buffet. I loved having a mimosa in the morning! The best thing was that the cocktail hour food was amazing and changed significantly each day. At both main services they had a wonderful selection of very fine cheeses. The afternoon tea had a nice array of nibbles, too. They seemed to be a bit slow in the service in the lounge, but most of the time i think it was cultural and not wanting to intrude or to seem pushy...I loved the amenities in the room especially the nice sound system and the soothing Chinese Tea when we arrived. The bathroom was beautiful, though I do wish the tub and the shower had been a bit bigger. Each were fine only for one person really.As far as some of the otehr aspects of the hotel: We had a couple's massage in the spa's couple's suite and the service there was impeccable. The massage was one of the best each of us has had. The food from room service was surprisingly good, as was the food at Melt. We didn't try the other restaurants though we heard good things about the Japanese restaurant and the Mediterranean restaurant from friends staying at the same time as us. I sat out by the pool, but I didn't get in because the one day i had time I felt it was too cool to get wet and there is no hot tub. Overall, we really loved our stay at the Oriental, and we would go back in a heartbeat, particularly for the reasonable prices we had for the club (about $300 US after taxes/service fee).  
<Date>Sep 15, 2007

<Author>alauns1
<Content>Lovely food but overstaffed We stayed at the hotel for 3 nights and the over service nearly drove us crackers. The room was lovely, the views great, facilities turn down etc great but the hotel is overstaffed to the extent that it is inefficient.You are greeted by 3/4 staff on going in for breakfast, then brought to a table by one of the staff where you order coffee/tea etc before helping yourself to a wonderful buffet. Obviously the desk then process the check to sign and deliver it to the table independent of the serving staff and one morning we received the check to sign before we had even got our coffees!!!!We dined one night in the japanese restaurant which was very good but to give an example of the staff not being busy enough, we ordered water and during the course of the meal the waiter would visit the table, open one bottle of water, pour it into one glass, replace the cap, replace the bottle on the table...open the other bottle of water, pour it into the other glass, replace the cap, replace the bottle.......wait a few minutes watching how much you have drunk and repeat the process.There were other examples of 3 people from reception dealing with the same thing, 3 people hovering for the bags on check out.....again more staff is not necessarily better.We like good 5 star service, but service should be unobtrusive. This hotel is over staffed and fussy because of it.

<Author>Bonnie84
<Content>Out of this world Wow! What an amazing start to a holidayMy partner and I booked a trip to Austalia and as the journey is a long one we decided to stop over in Singapore for a few nights.Not knowing what Singapore was like let alone the hotels we took a gamble and chose The Oriental Hotel - the pictures looked amazing on the website so we thought why not!We arrived and I must say the pictures were great but nothing compared to the real thing! On arrival our bags were taken to our room which was the Premier city suite, and we got shown round the hotel by the staff. The hotel is faultless, the decor is amazing and completley compliments what the hotel is offering. The swimming pool is amazing which also has a childs pool too. Our hotel room was amazing totally out of this world, the bathroom was huge, plenty of strorage and a lovely comfy bed. What was a nice surprise was that as we was on one of the suite floors we had complimentary breakfast and evening canapes, all of which was fantastic and on our very own floor!!! What I loved about the hotel was how friendly people were, very helpfull and always smiling - just what you want when you are on holiday. The hotel was very very clean and we felt like royalty!The choice of restaurants was brilliant to, there were plenty to choose from continental, japanese, tai, american etc. The hotel is very very close to the harbour and shopping malls and is a 5 minute taxi journy to the local markets and orchard road. I felt that Singapore was very cheap but if you want to spend big bucks then head to Orchard Rd where all the boutique shops are - if your looking for something traditional, a bargain or electrical items at a great price then head to the markets at china town! In my opinion the price of the Hotel was very cheap considering what you pay for a basic hotel in England what you get at the oriental is loads for your money. If your thinking about going here then I would definatley recommend booking one of the delux, or premier suites as breakfast is thrown in (but double check before booking) !Overall the hotel and the area was spot on - we will be definatley be returning to this hotel - 10 out of 10!

<Content>Fabulous Oriental We have just returned from 4 nights at the Oriental Hotel Singapore. We loved staying here, the hotel was fabulous and the service outstanding. We had a standard room which was very spacious (bigger than we had expected) and ample space for 2 adults and our 2 year old (who slept in a cot provided by the hotel). What makes this pool area even better is the staff, the greet you as you walk out to the pool, have your towels ready on your cabana chair (with a headrest!), then they bring you a bottle of cold water and a small plate of fresh fruit. They have kids pool toys as well so our little one was entertained. Very relaxing. My husband had a massage in the day spa which was fantatsic. We didn't eat at any of the restaurants apart from breakfast but they did seem lovely. Overall we loved this hotel for the staff, the tranquil surrounds and being on the marina (with a shopping centre right next door). It was excellent (and just far away from the bustle of Orchard road but close enough to everything). It was fabulous with a toddler too who loved going up and down in their glass lifts. We would definately recommend this hotel and stay here again.

<Author>S_G.UK
<Content>Good for Suntec The Oriental has 1) beautiful communal areas, folllowing a recent renovation, that give the traveller a lovely sense that they have arrived in Asia - great, esp if it is your first time in S'pre or the region. 2) great staff. Friendly, attentive, and absolutely everywhere you look. Rooms are pretty standard 'could be anywhere in asia' affairs but large, with nice bathrooms and comfy beds. Location near Suntec, Raffles etc is nice - there's really only 2 places to stay in S'pore if you want the 'big international hotel' thing and that's at Suntec or on Orchard Road. To be honest, taxis are so easy to get and cheap and the city so small, I wouldnt have a problem with not being on or near Orchard Road.

<Author>EfJay
<Content>Nice room to sleep, but doing anything else expensive I say up front we are not usually 5 star people - but we booked the Oriental as a special treat for the first 2 nights of a 2 week holiday after we flew into Singapore. It also coincided with our wedding anniversary.We booked an ocean view double on line directly with the hotel - but upon arrival found we were 'upgraded' to a Harbour View twin (2 beds pushed together) due to the hotel being at 'full occupancy'. A bit disappointing, given the fact that we booked the room  had it confirmed by the hotel months before.The room itself was lovely, the pillows and bed the most comfortable I have ever slept on and the view from L12 superb - but I would rather have had the double room we had on our confirmation email. Still it was nicely appointed with good quality fittings, robes, towels, toiletries etc.We found everything outside the room was beyond our budget. Even the online rate (quoted on line in $USD different for each night) was converted to a common $SGP rate per night on arrival - presumably averaged out over the 2 nights. We had to sign our agreement to check in, leaving me wondering if we were being ripped off as I was not familiar with the $USD/$SGD/$AUD exchange - have to wait for the credit card bill to check! The shops  restaurants in the surrounding area were also expensive and quiet, and lacking in the genuine street life which for me is part and parcel of Asia. I found the location out of the way - the hotel we stayed at on previous visit (Meritus Mandarin) and later on our holiday (Oxford) were much better locations. We tried to get a drink at the round bar on level 4 but it was crowded and the door people asked us to wait (!!)so we headed out of the hotel for all of our food and drink after that. The foyer was beautiful but I found it rather dark and gloomy - no natural light at all. The final bill was $600 SGD including tax but no breakfast - we didnt do anything in the hotel at all other than sleep. I agree with others that the reception area was always busy and you felt like you being railroaded when you went there for anything.In short, if you actually go to see the city - and not hang about the hotel room - there are far better value options!

<Author>Gifford
<Content>Not a patch on the Oriental Bangkok My husband and I stayed here for 6 nights in April and I have to say that compared to the standards of service set by the Oriental Bangkok we were disappointed.At check in they seemed only interested in upgrading us to a Club room at an extra cost of about 拢70/night. This seemed over the top and we felt that a 5* hotel should have been more interested in welcoming us than trying to make a quick buck. On top of this we felt food and drink in the hotel was overpriced (drinks were actually cheaper in Raffles Hotel). We went to Morton's bar one night only to be told we could only have one drink as they were closing. My cocktail was the worst and most expensive Cosmopolitan I have ever had. This is clearly a business-orientated hotel and there were a few conventions on when we visited which made the dining room busy at breakfast time.Despite these criticisms the hotel is very well situated for seeing the sights of the city and the room was very nice, though again not quite up to its Bangkok counterpart, though that hotel is in a class of its own.For anyone already booked to stay here do not worry, the hotel is still very good, but I do not think it is up to the many rave reviews previously given, as there are many excellent hotels in Singapore

<Author>Belgian_EU
<Content>Amazing hotel This was an amazing hotel, one of the best I have stayed in. The service was 95% excellent - only once did they forget to come and collect my laundry.The hotel upgraded me to a Harbour View room on the 12th floor and the view was magnificent. The room was new, although without a LCD TV, but it had cables for connecting iPods to the surround-sound system and a DVD player. The bathroom was huge and well-appointed. The bed was king-sized and extremely comfortable. Breakfast had been included and the buffet on the 4th floor had everything I would expect from a 5 star hotel in Asia.The only downside was the location, as the hotel faces the developments on the harbour. It is a good 15 minutes on foot to the nearest MRT at the moment (City Hall) although this will improve when the Circle Line is finished. However you can cross the road to the Esplanade and there is a bus stop. Thank goodness taxis are so cheap in Singapore!

<Author>randcbathgate
<Content>A good stay at about the Oriental BUT ... My husband and I stayed here for 4 nights in April. Having stayed a week previously at the Mandarin in KL (see our review) where the service was really fantastic, the Oriental was a little disappointing by comparison. The public areas and hotel rooms are exactly what you would expect from a hotel of this class. Rooms were spotlessly clean and well serviced. Toiletries and tea/coffee were replenished twice daily, and fresh fruit was put into the room each morning.There was a good roof top pool area with sun loungers, (but not enough umbrellas), and a spa which was very nice. The hotel also benefits from being located next to the Marina Mall - which can be accessed from the hotel forecourt.Location wise the Oriental is great. You are walking distance from the old Colonial areas of the city (Raffles landing point etc) and taxis are plentiful around the hotel.The downside to this hotel was the service. Whilst everyone was very polite, it was obvious that this is a hotel with a high turnover of guests. During our stay there were a number of conferences underway at the hotel, and also endless tour buses delivering, or collecting guests. This meant that reception was always busy, and you generally had to wait to speak to reception staff/concierge.When we were intially show to our room the receptionist left very quickly, and did not explain any of the room features. The tv/audio system was quite complicated to work and we would have appreciated them spending a little time to explain this. We had drinks in two of the hotels bars. On both occasions the sevice was very slow, despite neither bar being particularly busy.These are really minor points, and the hotel overall was a great base for our stay. We would recommend it.

<Content>extremely dissapointed! Having stayed at some of the better hotels in the far east, we thought that we would be on a safe bet by booking the oriental club rooms, for our 3 day stay. <Author>firebucket
<Content>Sensational Singapore!! : ) We stayed at this wonderful hotel in early March '07 for 4 nights, after booking through asia best hotels for $210 SIN per night including full buffet breakfast. At this price it presented as excellent value for money - (included +++).About S$15 for a taxi from Changi Airport direct to the hotel (cheap), where check-in was very friendly and a complete breeze. However, when we went to the deluxe city view room on the 7th floor, we discovered the configuration was 2 x twin double beds. Not much good for our 1st year wedding anniversary! After checking our paperwork from the internet booking company, I found the mistake had been mine, erroniously ticking twin instead of double!! Oooops. (Had done the same for our next hotel in Phuket also! Double ooops)Back we went to the reception desk, cap in hand, to try and get a king bed room. Well, I think the poor girl may have thought the mistake was their's as we were upgraded to the Grand City View room which is about 49 sqm and USD $320 pn on their website. Beautiful.She personally escorted us up to the 9th floor to ensure we were happy with the room (which we were!) and left us to settle in. The room was massive with a seperate sitting/lounge area, huge balcony, seperate dressing area and massive dark marble bathroom. It had all the usual trappings of a 5 star hotel with Wireless high speed internet access, Cable television, work desk, Dual-line telephones with IDD and voicemail, Bathtub and a separate glass enclosed shower, Plush terry-towelling bathrobes and slippers,Tea and coffee making facilities, Hair dryer and mini bar  Daily selection of local and international newspapers. The only thing that could possibly be improved on would be the brightness of the lighting in the bathroom area (mirror), which I found a little dim. This hotel is really quite beautiful inside with a stunning internal atrium area and glass elevators. The decor is unmistakeably asian with dark hues and huge chandelliers. The pool area is what you would expect with a 25 metre lap pool and adequate gym area. Only missing a hot spa! The pool attendants quickly  happily set you up with a lounger, plush pool towels  free bottled water. (The hotel provided several free bottles of mineral water in your room also).Breakfast was the most comprehensive that I have ever seen - anywhere. On the first day we wondered in all of it was really included in the price we had payed. Definately try to get it included because it costs about S$45 per person if you pay on the day. They had there own little bakery cooking anything you wanted, eggs done anyway you liked, fresh squeezed juices in front of you etc etc etc... It really has too many food choices to list here, but you could never get bored with it and the service was just great and so quick. The location of the hotel is perfect. The Marina shopping centre it is attached to is one of the best we found in Singapore really. (MRT Station, great Restaurants, a bowling alley, cinemas and all the shops you could want.) The Merlion was an easy walk, river boat tours, fountain of wealth and Raffles Hotel. Watch those Singapore Slings though at S$44 for two at Raffles! But you gotta do it! We tried the MRT a couple of times but honestly the cabs are so very reasonable in price we just caught them in the end or walked. The night safari is a must-do and we enjoyed that immensely. We just caught a cab there and back from the Oriental which was under S$20. We really loved Singapore in general, the Oriental Hotel and would love to go back sometime soon.

<Author>David in Manchester
<Content>Loved this Hotel Well I had stayed in Singapore before at a great hotel - The Intercontinental - but I thought I should try somewhere diferent and I cerftainly was not disapointed. This hotel is great. I booked a room on the Club floor with a harbour view. (Next time I'd go for a City view. The rooms are a bit bigger, they're slightly cheaper and the harbour view isn't anything that special to look at. Just lots of rusty old ships queing up!).The room was great. A bathroom with a full lenght window into the bedroom which could be closed off with a wooden venetian blind. The only minor criticism is that if you like a bath then the bath's a bit small. The rooms are very nicely furnished and I could even plug my iPod into the room's music system. There's two pieces of free ironing/pressing a day included in the rate so if you're clothes are creased after travelling no problem.The Club room was great. A fantastic breakfast with Moet Chandon, complimentary tea, coffee and soft drinks served all day, afternoon tea and cocktails with nibbles served for two hours in the evening. The nibbles were fantastic. One day Chinese, one day Indian etc. If you don't eat very much you wouldn't need dinner!The staff were extremely helpful and attentive.No adverse comments about this hotel. I would certainly recommend it!

<Author>menome
<Content>Very nice hotel This hotel seems small at first, the reception area is not all too big, you could call it cosy. Check in was prompt and we did get a free upgrade to a junior suite for no apparent reason. The service is excellent, they are quite patient at the front desk and you never have to wait long before someone attends to you. The bell boys are excellent as well, they did the small things that really add up and make it from a good to an excellent experience. You have people with specialise jobs, ie. the hail taxi man, the luggage boys, the laundry lady, so there was always people to attend to you very promptly for your every need. The rooms were very nice, I think the hotel must of recently got refurbished. Seperate shower and bathtub, large bathroom; room overall was a good size. Breakfast, room service or any type of food or service (especially food) was very expensive at this place. The supermarket is literally 2 minute walk from hotel in Marina square shopping centre so no need to use the hotel snacks. The Tiger beer in fridge was out of date, but that is the only flaw I could find in this hotel for my 5 nights stay. Overall, this was an excellent hotel and out of the 5 star hotels my travel agent showed me, this was in fact the cheapest option but turns out to be one of the best hotels I've stayed at.

Now my son and I are in a large pleasant room with living area and balcony and a nice view of the singapore skyline.Rooms are very clean and beds very comfortable.Room service is excellent, efficient and reasonably priced-just as well as we have been confined to the room for a few days!IT facilities are excellent and internet access good value.You are spoilt for choice at breakfast in the Melt cafe and service is perfect-no need to ask for coffee refills here!Haven't tried any other restaurant yet but good selection.Location is good and I would prefer to stay in this Marina area than Orchard road area.Shopping mall attached to hotel that connects to several other malls and city MRT station.Looking forward to travelling on and joining my husband and daughter but will be sad to leave the Oriental.Will definitely stay here when return to Singapore!

<Content>Not so great Slightly disappointed! Nothing special.Pool are area was good, but something was missing there as well, it was not a five star hotel standard, it was moreless 4-star hotel pool.I liked the deco of the hotel, but on some rainy days, I felt that it's a bit dark and gloomy, maybe the wall-to-wall carpets or something should be changed to make it a bit brighter. Coming down from the 21st floor and looking out of the elevator I didn't feel it looks like a 5-star hotel. The (small) reception area is stylish though.All in all, a good experience, but I don't think I'll stay another time.

<Author>Shermanator
<Content>True Royal Treatment Wow sums up this hotel nicely. We booked one of the Club Experience rooms, which included access to the Oriental Lounge on the 19th floor and lots of other extras. Free airport pick up in a Mercedes set the tone for the next two nights stay perfectly. From the minute we stepped out of the car at the hotel, we were treated like true VIPs. We were whisked up for a quick tour of the club loubge, then taken directly to our room to check in with Alice, one of the impeccable front desk staff. The room was gorgeously decorated, the bed super comfortable, and the entertainment system very good. A sumptuous breakfast, afternoon tea and evening cocktails with nibbles were served in the lounge, which boast a very nice view- and all complimentary. Be warned, however, that the hotel enforces a smart casual dress code in most of its public places. This meant that no flip flops or shorts, for example, were allowed in the lounge or even in Morton's bar for a quick drink. This was a bit of a nuiscance, being that the outside temperature was about 30c, so we had to change a couple of times. The pool does not have very many sun loungers, so get there early.We would highly recommend this hotel- the staff bend over backwards to be helpful, and are always very friendly and curteous.

<Author>popeye3
<Content>Wonderful Experience My wife and I stopped here for five nights (end of November/early December) and the experience was wonderful. We took the Club Room option which was well worth the money. We were checked in in the room and were greeted with fresh flowers, fruit and a bottle of wine - fantastic. We have never stayed at a hotel with so many curteous staff available to do your bidding, nothing was too much troubleWe tried the Club Room for breakfast on the first morning and it was very nice but the choice was limited. We then switched to the Melt Cafe (at no extra cost) which was little less than astounding, such an amazing choice of food and all well cooked and presented. Again the staff were efficient and attentive. We only managed Afternoon Tea in the Club Room once and it was very nice but limited to small cakes and tea/soft drinks etc. Unfortunately we never made it for coctails and canapes in the evening.We would advise paying the extra for the Club perks which in our case was good because it meant we didn't have to check out until 8pm which was useful since our flight was at midnight.This may or not be of interest but when we arrived at Changi Airport from the UK we looked at using the Shuttle Taxi to the hotel. The normal price is S$7 per person but we were told that we would have to wait up to an hour for a shuttle. They then tried to persuade us to take a shuttle for just the two of us at a cost of S$35 which they could provide immediately - what a con! We eventually got a taxi which cost S$15. The moral of the story is don't even think about getting the Shuttle just get a taxi - it's cheaper and quicker.In summary, if we go to Singapore again we will most definitely stay at the Oriental and wil be advising family and friends to do so as well.  
<Date>Dec 8, 2006

<Author>Roberto_NW_Italy
<Content>No question, it's a great hotel Had to stay there last night -at the airline's expense- 'cause my flight had been canceled. It was a genuine consolation!Stunning, well appointed and spacious room (although my views were not in the best direction), with hi fi TV system, huge window and own discreet terrace. Large marble bathroom, with quality towels, bath robe, slippers etc (those details are how I discern what is for me a great vs a just good hotel). Al;though there are a number of different restaurants, I ended up having both breakfast and lunch at The Cafe on the 4th floor. I had the best Nasi Goreng ever! Splendid presentation, ingredients and taste! That would be my lunch suggestion. Although I suspect many guests will also be amazed by the Asian/contemporary decor.Not unpredictably for such standard hotel, all the (many) staff I encountered were most kind and attentive, many really making efforts to go the extra mile to satisfy the customer.Good 25m swimming pool (with good service, big towels, complimentary water, refreshing sun spray, sun creams if you don't have yours etc), close to a small but well equipped fitness room (all Technogym machines).Caters wonderfully for anybody, just make sure you're OK with the location (not quite central to the main shopping areas, although e.g. Suntec City mall is at easy walking distance). It's the best of the four hotels I've tried so far in Singapore (others being, in my ranking order, Meritus Mandarin, Marriott, and Hilton).

<Author>Chalky9
<Content>Almost perfect, but... My wife and I stayed at the Oriental for one night following a cruise on the Star Flyer. Our room overlooked the pool and the harbour, with an extensive view slightly spoiled by construction work on the opposite side of the road.The room was a good size, very comfortable and offered everything you could want, including space to lay both our suitcases open. The marble bathroom had a large separate shower and was beautifully appointed, but the sliding door was very difficult to close. Soundproofing in the room was not as good as might have been expected, either from internal plumbing noises or external traffic and construction.The staff were excellent. We ate dinner in The Melt World Cafe which offered an extremely extensive self service buffet encompassing dishes from India, China, Thailand, Japan and the West, or a la carte. (This is also where the extensive breakfast buffet is laid out.) The food was good but the wine prices were frightening - the cheapest bottle on the list was 60 Singapore dollars, with most nearer 90! We had planned to eat in Mortons Steakhouse, but found on arrival that the dress code is semi-formal, which we weren't! In any case, a small steak was $S 73, which was more than the entire meal in The Melt.The location is fine if you want to be near Suntec, but not really in the centre of things. Overall we preferred the Marriott.

<Author>R8SKM
<Content>5 Star Service For Families Too Spent 10 nights here in October in a City view suite. The hotel made our family very welcome and both children (3  9) were left a small gift in the room on arrival.Our suite was immaculate and huge at 75 sq meters. A harbour view would have been even better - maybe next time!Paying extra for the club facilities is worthwhile and the hotel organised a baby sitter for us (at a very reasonable S$20/hour) so we could take advantage of the cocktails and canapes in the early evening.Complaints? Well, maybe I'm being a little picky but breakfast at The Melt restaurant - whilst excellent - could feel a little rushed given the number of people. On two occasions, I was presented with the bill to sign just as I sat down to eat - not what you need first thing!We had room service a couple of times and the food and service were excellent. You can walk to Marina Square in 3 minutes where there is a supermarket for those essentials (cheap wine!). In addition to a huge range of shops there too, check out the food court on the top floor. We sat outside with superb curries for us, pizza and ice cream for the children, two tiger beers and a superb view of Boat Quay and the city skyline.Singapore is a viable destination for young families. We did Sentosa, East Coast Park, the Night Safari and Chinatown. Both children really enjoyed the holiday and the staff at the pool where excellent too.Would we return? Absolutely, especially if we are upgraded to a harbour view suite next time!

After reading all of the reviews, I had a very hard time choosing a hotel. When I approached my husband, he came up with the idea of staying at a couple of hotels, each for three or four nights. We ended up staying at The Oriental, The Ritz Carlton, The Shangri-la, and The Sentosa Resort and Spa. The Oriental was by far the unanimous favorite. Our stay at the Oriental was phenomenal. The accommodations were exquisite, but more importantly the service was unmatched by any other hotel in Singapore. We stayed in a city suite with club access. We booked the Suite Success package, which included a luxury airport transfer. We were actually arriving by ferry, and the hotel was very nice and willing to pick us up at the ferry terminal. When we exited the ferry terminal (along with 150 other passengers) we greeted by name by the driver (don't ask me how he knew who we were, we are still puzzled over that one) and transferred by Mercedes to the hotel. Upon arriving at the hotel, we were greeted at the steps of the hotel (once again by name) by a very kind lady. She immediately showed us right up to our room where she checked us in. She also provided to us a letter that detailed all of our included amenities during our stay. (This was a very nice touch, since often times you miss out on things that were actually included, because you didn't ask.) Staying in the City Suite was a little more expensive, but well worth the extra money. The extra benefits we received practically paid for themselves. Access to the club lounge, complimentary laundry pressing service, late checkout in the club lounge, fresh fruit, complimentary internet access, and a gigantic room made us feel like we were royalty. There was even an extra 1/2 bath that was convenient when you have a spouse that hogs the bathroom. Every single employee of the hotel went out of their way to accommodate all of our needs. After a long day at the Singapore Zoo we arrived about 10 minutes late for hors d鈥檕euvres in the club lounge. We decided to go up to the lounge anyway to get a drink. Upon arrival to the lounge, we were seated and told that they had just put away the food, but she would fill us up a plate in the kitchen (with a little of everything) and bring it to us. She went out of her way, and it made all the difference.When it was time to checkout and move on to the next hotel, we didn鈥檛 want to leave. For the next 8 days, while staying at the Ritz Carlton and Shangri-la, everything was just okay. Yes, these other hotels are very nice, but compared to the service we received at the Oriental, they were disappointing. My advice to you is, stay at the Oriental. If you are determined to compare the other hotels, just make sure to make the Oriental the last hotel you stay in, because everything else dulls in comparison to the service you receive at the Oriental. Don鈥檛 do what we did, and spend the rest of your trip saying, 鈥淲ell, at the Oriental 鈥︹€︹€?When we return to Singapore, we will definitely return and stay the entire trip at The Oriental.

<Author>Sydney-AP
<Content>Ok Business Hotel but not great Having read all the reviews on Tripadvisor I tried the Oriental in both Club and standard rooms. Its a really pleasant business hotel, the club facilities are excellent with the most delightful staff and fit out. The breakfast is superb. The rooms are fine even if its a little obvious that they are older style hotel rooms that have been renovated tastefully eg old joinery with new soft furnishings. The pool area is nice but again its obviously an old hotel that has been renovated. The service is delightful, genuine and warm but its an old hotel dressed up to be something it no longer is - that doesn't make it an adequate member of the Oriental group. Don't let me make it out to be terrible which it isn't - what it isn't is a cohesive first class experience.

<Author>graceC
<Content>Would stay there again in a heart beat We stayed at The Oriental during our recent trip to Singapore in Sept/Oct 2006. We first stayed there for 3 nights, then flew to Jakarta for a few days, and came back to The Oriental Singapore for 8 more nights. We booked everything through AMEX that gave us a good deal.Before arrival, we have exchanged emails with the hotel to confirm and reconfirm our booking. Our reserved room was for Deluxe Oceanview room. We also inquired about their airport transfer services and was told it would cost Sing$60 one way with a Mercedez Benz 200 series. We decided to take a cab instead since they're plenty available in Singapore and cheaper too. We arrived with bleary eyes @ 1am at the hotel after a 20-hour flight from Chicago. At first glance, the lobby was quite modern looking with marble surface all around and some water fountains that created that soothing feeling as we entered. I think they just renovated the hotel recently because everything still looked new. The check-in staff was courteous, friendly, and very helpful. To our delightful surprise, they told us that our room has been upgraded to a Club Level Harbour View room. However, my husband wanted to try out their suite since we knew both of us would be suffering from jetlag for the next few days so it would help to have a separate living room so that when one of us couldn't sleep, one could watch TV in another room without bothering the other. We got our suite on the 18th floor with Sing$190 extra per night which included all the Club Floor amenities (upgraded champagne breakfast for 2, fresh flowers and fruits daily, free internet access at the lounge, late afternoon cocktail with snacks, and guaranteed late checkout until 8pm). The suite was spacious and whistle clean with marble surface all around and modern contemporary design, a living room with step-out balcony and a decent size restroom with double sinks as well as study desk with leather desk amenities + high-speed internet access hookup, the bedroom has an armoire with TV, DVD player, video player, and one touch control from the night stand and big window for the water view, it also has big bathroom (all marble) with separate bathtub / shower / commode / double vanity area. The next day, we went to check their Champagne breakfast at the executive lounge and didn't like the selections (it mostly offers western types of breakfast) so we went down to 'The Melt Cafe' that has better choices with local taste. We asked that our breakfast be switched to 'The Melt' instead of the Champagne Breakfast (I dislike alcohol so I can't imagine drinking Champagne first thing in the morning with your breakfast!), and our request was granted without problem. The Melt buffet breakfast offers several dining stands: fresh fruit stand with a guy ready to help cut up your tropical fresh fruit selections or juice them for you, dessert stand, bakery stand, eggs/noodles stand with chinese dim-sum and sliced meat, american breakfast stand that has the usual bacon / omelet / scrambled eggs stuff, Indian cuisine stand, Malay cuisine stand that has Malay's Nasi Lemak and Chinese style porridges, and continental breakfast stand. Each stand offers roughly 10-15 choices of food so you'll definitely find one that you like. It has friendly and great customer service, fast, clean, and everything was run efficiently.During our stay for the second time, out jetlag was over so we decided to stick with our original reservation (Deluxe Oceanview Room) and again we got upgraded to the Club Level Harborview room on the 16th floor. We still received our fresh flowers and fresh fruits daily although we no longer received the club level amenities. That's fine since we were out most of the time anyway.The room was almost identical in layout minus the separate living room and the second restroom. All the amenities were the same as the ones we got at the suite (terry bathrobes, slippers, nice size shampoos / conditioners / bathgels, toothbrushes, sewing kit, cotton balls and sticks, soaps, etc). Everytime we went down to the lobby, there were always a few staff available to either help with the elevators or any other help you needed (even when the check-in desk was crowded there were always staff available to help you immediately). The room-service was always fast with the food delivered still hot and delicious. The staff was knowledgeable about their country and its places of interest. The hotel is situated next to Marina Square, a dept store with great food court on the 3rd floor. You can also go across the street to the Esplanade and do a bit of walking along the panoramic Singapore river bank. When we checked out this time, our flight back home wouldn't leave until 10.00pm so we requested a late checkout @ 7.30pm and it was granted free of charge without problem.All in all a 5-star experience all the way.

<Author>Clancie
<Content>Brilliant service at The Oriental I stayed at The Oriental with my husband and 5 y.o. son in OCT 06. We had a fantastic (although short) stay, enjoying the best hotel service we have ever experienced. The staff are nothing short of amazing - this is an extremely well run hotel. The rooms are very large; ample space for a king size bed and a rollaway bed. (We were charged no extra for the rollaway). The buffet breakfast at the hotel is incredible - try to get this included in your room rate, otherwise it is very expensive. The hotel is positioned over the top of the Marina Square shopping centre - providing easy access to air conditioned shopping, as well as a range of restaurants. I would highly recommend The Oriental Hotel in Singapore - I could not fault this property in any way.

<Content>Highly recommended My wife and I stayed in a triple room with our teenage daughter: we were very impressed.Staff were unfailingly polite and helpful, including allowing us early access to our room after arriving directly from a 12-hour flight from Europe. The room was stylish and very quiet, reasonably spacious and the beds were very comfortable. The bathroom (marble, separate shower and bath) was stocked with quality accessories. <Author>wendybatch
<Content>fantastic hotel As others have said, this really is an amazing hotel. From the moment we arrived we were subjected to perfect, old fashioned service in a fantastic hotel.We upgraded to the club rooms which turned out to be a good choice. We didnt need it, but it includes a late check out till 8pm! This represents great value for money. The room includes all the usual drinks and food daily , including a really good champagne between 5 and 7pm, and wireless internet access on your laptop. Nothing is too much trouble for the staff.We went to visit Raffles hotel for afternoon tea but couldnt get in and it didnt look that great anyway. Was most disappointed in the hotel which is an institution in Singapore. We came back and had afternoon tea in the Oriental which was great value at 8 UK pounds and included a chocolate fountain with fruit and marshmallows my husband had great fun with!!Breakfast at Melt, as everyone else has already said is quite simply the best. The fruit station was my favourite with every fruit you could think of and some, which they would juice just for you. Fantastic!Taxis are cheap and plentiful and you can walk along the riverfront into town quite easily, we did it at night and it was really lovely. All in all an amazing hotel which I cannot really fault. Stay here!!!

<Author>Maillot-Jaune
<Content>Very impressed! Stayed at the Oriental twice in August at either end of a trip to Thailand. We booked the hotel following the consistenty positive reviews read on Tripadvisor and we would have to say that we were very impressed. We booked a city view room, but on the first stay were upgraded to a Harbour View room and on the second stay an Ocean View room.There is some construction work going on next door but we did not notice any major noise or disruptions.We didn't eat at the hotel restaurants to be honest so can't comment on those. The adjoining shopping centre is really good, with quite a few eating options, and there is also an outdoor hawker market across from the hotel on the Esplanade. The breakfast though is simply awesome, (we had it included in our room rate - very much recommended) we have been lucky enough to have done a fair bit of travelling in the last 10 years or so and we have stayed in other 5 star hotels in a number of countries, including a previous stay in Singapore and the breakfast at the Oriental is by far the best experienced. The choice of food, from Indian (may sound strange but boy it was good) to freshly made pancakes (my wifes favourite) is fantastic.The service was also faultless, and genuine too from our experience. For example on one occasion I went to reception to arrange a late checkout and taxi to the airport. The reception area was really busy and I realised that it was 11am when quite a few people were checking out, so I thought I'd leave it till later. On the way back to the lifts, a member of staff approached me who had noticed that I had wanted something but had left. She rode up in the lift with me, made a note of what I required and called our room 30 mins later to confirm late checkout, taxi booking and alarm call. I was very impressed by that.The gym is also pretty good and the pool is nice although I must say the pool area is fairly bland and could maybe do with more gardening perhaps. There is a good view from the pool area though.The hotel seemed very interested in customer comments and feedback and I would assume based on our experience that they are acting on this response.In summary we would not hesitate to return to this hotel.

<Author>merry_party
<Content>Enjoyed our stay at the Oriental! We stayed at the Oriental 2 nights in July and 3 nights in August. Both stays were enjoyed by all. July was with our two children, and we paid for a City View rooms. We asked for connecting rooms and got that plus an upgrade to Water Views room for both. The decor was subdued Oriental: ivory, black, beige, brown. The beds were perfect, as were the pillows, not too soft and not too firm. The sound system in the room was excellent (there was a subwoofer). The toilet and bath were marble, and there was a shower with an all glass door. A clear effort was made to make toilet plumbing as unnoticeable as possible, ie, the water closet was hidden behind a marble wall with a heavy marble lid (I know coz I tried to lift it).Our August trip was also for a City View room but we got upgraded to a Water View room (again!) as it was our second time. And we were lucky enough to catch the fireworks shows for the National Day in the comfort of our bedroom - what good timing!Both stays we opted for the buffet breakfast, and it was a fantastic way to start your day. The variety and quantity of food, as well as the service were excellent. I did notice though that the female wait staff were more prompt, and courteous than the male wait staff. The breakfast choices were: fruit juices and I was able to request for watermelon juice which they prepared for me; eggs any way you want it; pancakes and waffles with various toppings; Indian curries and breads; Chinese congee and dimsum; bacon, sausages, hash browns; croissants and pastries; yoghurt; cereal; plus many types of cut fruit. We also had room service for mains, and they added complimentary entrees, not a huge serving but a nice touch as it was individually presented as you would in fine dining.The outdoor pool was a great way to relax, the prices for alcoholic drinks were a bit steep though. About S$18 net.The Oriental is beside a shopping mall, and about S$5 to Orchard road by cab. So, if shopping is your main purpose for visiting Singapore, then the Oriental is convenient. We did our shopping in July for the sales. In August we decided to go for more sightseeing than shopping, and the Oriental's proximity to Suntec was a bonus. There were tour buses that started and ended at Suntec and it was easy for us to board whenever we wanted to. If we needed to go back to the hotel, we were in and out of Suntec in 30 minutes, which is when the buses come and go.The staff were very helpful, and courteous. Always with a greeting and a smile. We plan to stay with the Oriental whenever we go to Singapore and will not think twice about recommending it. What a wonderful hotel!

<Content>Disappointed We booked the hotel for a work retreat partly on the basis of the reviews here and I must say that we were somewhat disappointed. There were around 10 of us and I must say the service of the hotel was just not up to stratch.1. We arrived at the hotel around 6.30 pm and attempted to check in. This took 30 mins because some of our rooms were still not available. Given check out time is around midday, I find it somewhat strange that the rooms are still not available at that hour. 2. We had upgraded one of the rooms to the executive floor because they wanted to charge SG500 for the use of the room for a couple of hours. This charge seemed rather high given we had a group of 10 persons staying at their hotel - could they not offer us a discount? Anyway, by getting an upgrade we could use the executive floor facilities, which included free use of the room for 2 hours. But when we tried to check in, we were informed that there was no reckon of our upgrade, despite the fact that we had phoned up twice in advance to confirm.3. We got to the executive floor room, which really was just ordinary. It was a nice well decorated modern hotel room, but quite small for a 5 star hotel room. In fact, this room turned out to be smaller than another colleague's room, which was on the ordinary floor. Go figure. 4. On the whole, we did not find the staff to be very friendly. During check in, while the whole group was left waiting at the lobby, they could not even muster a smile or look apologetic about keeping us waiting. 5. The hotel is far from the city center. There is lots of shopping Suntec, but coming back from the city center does involve a cab ride, which during peak hour can be quite difficult to find (I've been told Singapore cabbies are prone to hiding waiting for people to call for bookings).On the other hand, the pool was lovely, as were the staff there. The Melt also has an awesome buffet. Given the number of other lovely, centrally located hotels, I do not think I would stay here again.

<Author>WestCanTraveler
<Content>Room with breakfast The highlight of the Oriental is its breakfast buffet--be sure to book a room that includes this breakfast in the price! (our special rate from the Mandarin Oriental hotel website included breakfast and late checkout)The rooms we had were in need of some modernisation, although the bathrooms seemed to have been upgraded more recently than the main area. Marble everywhere and a great power rain shower--and above average toiletries. The beds were not of the standard the Marriott and Westin now have made commonplace, although the linens were definitely luxe. TV had a wide range of channels. Service to the rooms was exceptional: fresh fruit left every day and at evening turndown, new towels and free bottled water. The breakfast buffet is huge and the quality like nothing else I've encountered (and I travel a lot). Wait staff have many, many tables to take care of, but do it all with ease and friendliness. I was much more impressed by them than by the reception staff who were very formal and frankly rather slow....Location is very good--a big mall adjoining, the Esplanade theatres and waterfront across the street, and less than 10 minutes walk to a wide range of restaurants including the lovely CHIJMES complex. Taxis were readily available outside the hotel and it's very cheap indeed to go anywhere in the city. I would definitely stay here again and for my children it was a memorable experience of a top-end hotel. This is a business hotel that makes families welcome too and it would likely suit all types of visitor.

<Author>Milkee
<Content>Great service - above average room We stayed at the Oriental in early July 06 for 4 nights as part of a 21 night Singapore - Thailand holiday. We arrived at the hotel at 11.00pm after a enjoyable flight from Australia. We were greeted by pretty much everyone in the foyer at the time of arrival. The lobby looks great at night. The service is brilliant.We were promptly escorted to our rooms and our bags arrived minutes later. We had asked about the Melt breakfast as our rate did not include it. We were told that it would be AUD $55 for both of us to have breakfast each day. We politely declined. If you can organise with your agent for a cheaper rate get it, otherwise, we found that there are plenty of places in Singapore that serve Kaya Toast (so good we brought two jars home with us) and coffee for two people for less than AUD $8. You just have to walk a little (less than 1 km). I reckon there was about 7 within the malls directly near the hotel. The best was at the Raffles Hotel cafe about just over 1 km walk (the one recommended in the lonely planet guide) through the numerous air-conditioned malls near the hotel.The rooms .... we stayed in a city view room. The view wasn't really of the city but of the back of Suntec Mall and another hotel. A little disapointing but i wasn't in the room to look at the view, you can do that on your adventures around the city. The bathroom is brilliant. The products in the room smell fantastic. The bath is massive and the shower was a rain shower and entirely marble. The rest of the room was a little dated for a 5 star hotel. I expected much better from the reviews on this website. The room was spotless, had a large floorspace and a good choice of TV channels (it had ABC Asia which showed an AFL game late one night!!!). It was nonetheless pleasant without being modern or over the top. The minibar prices were ridiculous but you expect that. The best part of the room is definitely the bathroom.Speaking of ridiculous, the prices of food within the hotel are outrageous compared to Australian prices and prices for other Asian hotel i have stayed in. For instance a steak will cost AUD $75+, 2 noodle/rice dishes and a chocolate desert cost us well over AUD$65 (room service), and alcoholic drinks of any description start around AUD$8-9. Needless to say, we only ate at the hotel for that one room service. Otherwise, go to Boat/Clarke quay, get a chilli crab (Brilliant!!!!!), pineapple rice, spring rolls and a few tiger beers/cocktails (with a perfect view) for around AUD$60-70 for 2. If you're fit you can walk it, if you can't be bothered a taxi will only cost about AUD$5-7. Lunch around the city is also very good and cheap. The pool is good. It has a beautiful view of the harbour but has the ambience of an empty olympic sized swimming pool. If you want it for the sole purpose of swimming after a long day at the shops or zoo it is perfect, but compared to other pools in Asia, it it would be very average but for the view. On the whole, it is a great hotel but food and drink is pricey by Australian and local Singapore standards. I probably wouldn't stay there again but only beacuse i would want to compare another hotel to this one. Having said that, i would definitely recommend it to anyone thinking of staying there. From reading the comments on this website, i would probably recommend you get the club room. From memory, it wasn't that much more per night and the breakfast/drinks/ canapes you consume would offset the initial payment.Btw, Singapore on the whole is brilliant (4 days and you can see it all). The zoo is a must, chilli crab is soooo good, shopping in the malls, whilst extensive, is as expensive as Australia so you will find that you only buy what you really want. Jewellery at the chinatown markets was cheap. Get on the MRT Trains, they are very clean and super quick and cheap. The lonely planet city guide was great for sightseeing, maps and tips.

<Content>Amazing Stay! Having read the reviews on this site we opted for a four night stay in club room.I cannot better the reviews the room was gorgeous, the service was fantastic the location excellent. Having read a few reviews on this site, I feared that the hotel was very business orientated an not the best location for sightseeing but in actual fact we found the location excellent, walking distance to Clarke and Boat Quay, Raffles, the Esplanade and Suntec mall ( and a base for hippo tours) was on the door step.If you are considering upgrading to the club room, I would highly recommend it, I love a cocktail or two in the evening before I go out and these were complementary, even the champagne cocktails (as opposed to the hundred S$60 it cost us for two at the bar). The breakfast included champagne, the afternoon tea was delightful and the canap茅s with the cocktails were excellent. The club lounge also provided the most amazing skyline views. If you are staying at the Oriental I would also recommend the Hawker stalls opposite the hotel at the theatres on the bay, the variety, quality and taste of the food was fantastic, as was the price. Also worth a recommendation is the bar on top floor of the Stamford hotel, the service was not that great but I have never seen a view quite like it. We really had an excellent stay, and couldn鈥檛 fault the hotel at all. Would recommend to everyone visiting Singapore, we can鈥檛 wait to go back.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Stay at The Oriental Stayed at The Oriental for 3 nights in May. I was very impressed with the hotel and service, but really began to appreciate it when I switched hotels to begin the business part of my trip (where I had no control over picking the hotel!).I opted for the airport pickup service from the Changi. When I arrived at the hotel, a check in person met me at the car and led me to my room. It was all very Bill Murray in Lost in Translation. Let me say one thing here-- I booked the absolute cheapest room rate via the Oriental website (113USD) so it's not like I was some VIP. We did the check in procedures in the room. The room itself was nice without being overly flashy. Even though I booked a normal room, they gave me a harbor view room, which was nice. It was the not very apparent features which I really liked. For instance, the bathtub had a can of sea salts, which I admit is something stupid to like as much as I did. I did, however, really like the fact that the hotel provided toothbrushes and razor kits. And an ironing board/iron. And an umbrella (which I didn't realize was there until I called the front desk to request the use of one for the day). The service was quite good. Taxis came immediately (which I didn't pay attention to until I kept having to wait 5 minutes for a taxi when I switched to The Regent). And the staff was helpful without being overbearing. I always got the good morning and good evenings, but they were never overly intrusive, which I have often found at other hotels. The spa was also very nice. I especially liked the small, semi-private relaxation beds they have for you after the treatments. I took a bit of a nap there after my massage/facial. I didn't eat much in the hotel, only the breakfast buffet at Melt. The food choice and quality was good. For me, the highlights were the selection of fresh juices and yogurt smoothies. While I was at the hotel, I thought it was great, but it was when I moved to The Regent that I realized just HOW great The Oriental is. The Regent, by any sane standards, is a good, if not great, hotel. But when directly compared to The Oriental, it falls short in every category. Just my opinion, of course.

<Author>yorkshirebonde
<Content>Amazing! An amazing hotel. Much enjoyed by myself and my husband. The trip was a combination of business (for him) and pleasure (for her) and once the business side of things was done we decided to book a different hotel from the company booked one for the rest of our stay. So glad we made the decision to change. Although the first hotel was good (Meritus Negara) and we have no complaints at all (we were upgraded to a suite), the extra effort from the staff at the Oriental made all the diference. The service from the staff was impeccable. All the way from check-in to settling into the room, to the staff in the club lounge to the doorman and concerge. Nothing was too much trouble. The domestic staff were polite and respectful of the privacy setting in the room. The front of house staff in the club lounge friendly with a sense of homour. On one occasion we were joking in the lift when one of the staff told him he should be proud to have such a problem i.e. me, (must remember to remind my husband of that on a regular basis!) We upgraded to a club room on arrival which was well worth the extra, champagne breakfast everyday, afternoon tea, and 2 hours of cocktails from 5.30 to 7.30pm all included. The club lounge was huge with stunning views over the city. The room itself was of a good size with all of the facilities you expect from a first class hotel. Even a point to plug to your ipod/mp3 player into the surround sound system in the room (cable supplied). I can recommend the spa there where I had 2 hours of bliss and was able to move my shoulders and neck in ways I hadn't done for years.  The only slight downside is the distance from the nearest MRT station, but it is a pleasant walk , all of which can be done under cover via the shopping malls. We'll certainly be staying there again given the chance.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful!! Stayed here November 2005 for 5 days, but wished we had longer. Fantastic hotel nothing was too much trouble. Can't wait to go again, maybe next year. We made a point to visit all gardens which are free and well worth the time. November is a good time as weather is good and not too busy. Buses were easy and taxis plentiful and cheap. Dont bother with western food get out onto the streets, everything is so clean and cheap so if its not to your taste, try the next place. We ate a lot of local food and always felt we were bursting with energy, never felt tired and always on the go, . Visit Mount Faber and Macritchie reservoir you will be glad you did, dont bother with the shops you can do that anywhere, get the metro and see the island. Little India is like the old Singapore( I was there in 1967. ) I re-visited my old home it looked small but apparently worth mega -bucks.As for hotel nowhere could be better situated and make sure you get a harbour view. Very reasonable rates usually 5 nights for 4 etc. If stopping over try to go for a 4 day trip. So much to see. We bookes through Kuoni and that was good (dont bother with Travel 2) If you're going that far you want a decent operator that you can communicate with.

<Author>KittyChan
<Content>MO S'pore: Beautiful Hotel with Bad Feng Shui? I stayed at the newly (and majorly) renovated Oriental in Singapore three times in 2005. The first time, in February, was very shortly after the hotel鈥檚 鈥渟oft鈥?reopening. Aesthetically, the redo is a huge success. While the hotel retains its rather nondescript exterior shape and square windows in a big white block of a building, the interior of the Oriental is now arguably the most striking of all hotels in Singapore. While most hotels built around an atrium recall the 80s even more pointedly than, say, Duran Duran cassette tapes and hair bands, the Oriental鈥檚 atrium is now dazzling, with mica-flecked black marble, pin-lighted water feature, and gorgeous dark woods everywhere. The staff are immaculate, the ladies in particular: their uniforms are very Singapore Airlines-meets-Asian Bond girls. As one often does in Singapore, I arrived very late in the evening and was tired. The Oriental鈥檚 sleek new interior and flawless staff immediately soothed. The front-desk clerk talked me into an S$90/night upgrade to a Club room, which turned out to be the same as a regular room but on a higher floor than my original room. Staff scurried in to replace stock MO amenities with Hermes, and someone else brought hot tea and a scented face towel. Aah. (Actually, the last two services come with all MO rooms.) The room, while smallish (34 m2), was beautiful: more dark woods and black marble, and an up-to-the minute bathroom with separate, walk-in rain shower; and glass wall with wooden blinds separating bed from bath rooms. My room had a dead-on view of Singapore鈥檚 harbor and attractive CBD skyline. Room service food was delicious and not overly expensive. Problems began the next morning (Saturday), when hammering and other construction noises began fairly early (shortly before 9 a.m.). I called the front desk to ask what was going on and was told that renovation work was still occurring on the uppermost floors 鈥?what would become the real Club rooms 鈥?and outside. I headed to the Club Lounge for breakfast, hoping that I might be able to sleep a bit more afterward. The lounge is brand new and spectacular: two-storey windows overlooking the city from the 21st floor, and rich yet muted Asian-modern d茅cor. The breakfast buffet was fresh, luxurious, and plentiful, including fairly good champagne (Piper-Heidsieck). Sated, I returned to my room and was able to sleep some more, as the construction crews had mercifully scaled down the pace and decibel level of their work Later in the day, I stopped by the front desk to discuss my concerns about the noises and what I thought had been a bit of a hard sell for a Club room that was only partly so. As is usually the case with MO staff I鈥檝e experienced in Asia, the duty manager was thoughtful and responsive. He took the supplemental club charge off of my room rate (for 2 nights), apologized for the noise, and assured me that I could move to another room if the work 鈥?scheduled for a shorter period 鈥?continued on Sunday. I went for a swim, and some laps the new pool put my cares behind me. The temperature-controlled infinity pool overlooks the city skyline, and the spa facilities and wet area are every bit as lovely as the rest of the hotel. When I returned to my room from my swim, I found a bottle of Shiraz and a very nice note from the duty manager, again apologizing for earlier problems.Sunday was just fine, with no construction noise and a good morning鈥檚 sleep. Upon returning home, I had a very nice e-mail from Ms Cindy Kong, the Oriental鈥檚 guest-relations manager. She again apologized for the problems I鈥檇 encountered and asked me to contact her directly concerning future stays to ensure proper care.I did contact Ms Kong again, as I was planning another visit to Singapore at the end of April and first week of May, bookends to a week in Bali. She assured me that construction work would be finished and that I would have an excellent, quiet room. That proved to be the case; this time I stayed in a Club room on the Club floor, and everything was great. I was looking forward to my return a week later. Ms Kong e-mailed me while I was in Bali to let me know that a new construction project (this time, a municipal endeavor at adjacent Marine Square) would be taking place during my anticipated stay, and she offered not only to help with a booking at another hotel but also to have me picked up upon arrival at Changi Airport and taken in an MO car to the alternate hotel. Again, MO鈥檚 outstanding customer service impressed.My third stay with the Oriental was in September, and this time the hotel offered me an ocean-view room at a very good rate. Unfortunately, I timed my stay to coincide exactly with a weekend of daylong F1 speedboat races 鈥?on the water, well within earshot of the hotel. I contacted the Front Desk, and staff offered to give me free use of a City Room, away from the water-facing sides of the hotel, for sleeping during the day. (I note here that the standard City rooms, while pleasant and comfortable, have noticeably blander d茅cor and furnishings than the Ocean and Harbor View rooms. Staff advised that City rooms are usually assigned to package-tour customers. In any event, my City day room was a blessed respite from the constant whining of racing speedboats.) I joked with the duty manager that perhaps I have bad feng shui at the Oriental, given my star-crossed stays to date. Unfortunately, the joke or bad FS continued a bit further: later on, while I was relaxing after the boat races in my Ocean room, a harsh chemical smell seeped into the room. I opened the door and the reek of kerosene in the hallway or similar brought tears to my eyes. I flagged down a maid, who reported that a maintenance worker had spilled paint in the storage room at the end of the hall and had dumped a large quantity of turpentine on the paint still to try to clean up. A few other guests had also been flushed out of their rooms, seeking the source of the fumes. I informed the front desk of the problem and then went for a long swim. When I returned to my floor, the paint-thinner odor had subsided a bit but was still fairly harsh. I had a message on my room voicemail from guest relations. When I called back, the duty manager apologized again and asked me whether the hotel could move me and my things to a City View suite. I readily agreed. The suite was wonderful 鈥?and huge (about 70 m2). Rather than replicating the drabness of the regular City rooms, the suite was very sleekly furnished and decorated, with a separate bedroom, two bathrooms, and expansive city views. Well done, Oriental! Oh, I had breakfast (included in my room rate) in the just-opened Melt restaurant, which has several huge food stations featuring dishes -- all fresh and very delicious -- from all over the world. The Indian station was my favorite for savories, and the Western breakfast-y baked goods were to die for.Although I鈥檝e not yet stayed again at the Oriental 鈥?I stayed at Raffles on my most recent trip to Singapore 鈥?I probably would stay there again. It really is a beautiful hotel, and the staff are perhaps the best I鈥檝e encountered (with the possible exception of those of Peninsula Hotels). I still attribute the problems I had at the Oriental to bad luck, or possibly bad feng shui, which perhaps one shouldn鈥檛 take lightly in a predominantly Chinese culture. Nonetheless, the Oriental richly deserves the very positive rankings and reviews it鈥檚 received since its very successful makeover. If one can get a good corporate or promotional rate (my cheapest stay was S$188/night), the Oriental may be the best hotel stay in Singapore.

<Content>My Taste Buds Melted.... Dr. Michael Lim The Travelling Gourmet is a renowned Travel, Food  Wine Writer in AsiaMELT the World Cafe at The Oriental Singapore melted my tastebuds....There are many mega-buffets now not only in sunny Singapore, but also in places like Hong Kong. <Author>Brunos
<Content>Very hot Oriental We did a brief night-stopover in Singapore on January 7th.We checked in around 7:40 pm (after a long trip from Europe)and left at 4am the next day. We were first given a room on the 16th floor. The room was hot when we got in and turned the air conditioner. By 9pm it had not cooled off, and we repeatedly called for engineering. They finally came and after an hour of work decided that it was not working. We were finally moved to another room on the 17th floor. The temperature was 27掳 when we came in and the manager turned the AC on. We directely went to bed but the AC did not work in this room either. Unfortunately we could not even open the window which was locked. It was midnight and did not have the courage to change room as we were to get up in less than four hours. Of course we got no sleep and the bell boy who picked up our luggage could attest that the temperature was over 27掳. The hotel looked almost empty and my guess is that the AC was closed on a few floors to save costs, but that the reception was not advised of it and gave us rooms on these floors. Whatever the reason, this is totally unacceptable from a five star hotel. I left a note of complaint to the hotel GM at checkout, but never got even a word of apologies. This tells a lot about the poor quality of management/service at this hotel. In Singapore there are many more reliable hotels.

<Content>Doesn't quite make it... I stayed at the Oriental over New year with my family. In my view it is still very much a 4 star hotel..The service is pretty good, and the location is excellent.. however certain key 5 Star attributes were missing:Our room was a little tatty - the electricity cupboard door was broken and exposed. Over all the place is very dark - both in the rooms (paticularly bathrooms) and in the lobby areas.Sadly there was very little pool service (ie. towels, beds, drinks). Most annoying however, was when the hotel decided that guests could not watch the New Year fireworks from the Swimming pool area without buying a ticket to a Champagne reception (no children allowed) - or go into a bar overlooking the marina without paying a New Years eve cover charge (no children allowed). Although we were 5 residents of the hotel, we were forced onto the street to see the fireworks.

<Author>sankar
<Content>Very Good, almost Great.... This is definitely a very nice hotel, though not perfect. But perhaps I had been expecting too much, considering the Mandarin Oriental Brand and what I had seen on their website. We took the standard rooms, which were pretty good in all respects but nothing very special. Big, bright, comfortable, a balcony would have been nice. And our room was a corner room which was weirdly shaped. The service was excellent, very friendly and helpful, they really go out of their way to help you. The Atrium lobby is nice but there are miles of boring white corridors on each floor which could've been spruced up with a little more color/decoration.The location is not the best, with few entertainment and late night dining options nearby, and the subway a long walk away. But it is right across the bay if you want a nice evening walk, and the bustling Boat Quay isn't too far away, and once you reach there the financial district is next door. Overall a great place to stay if you don't mind a slightly out of the way location.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Very Nice This hotel was very nice. I had a few problems with the service but overall it was a nice, clean hotel and good value for money. The rooms were on the small size and the views were not great and even after complaining that we did not like the view, we were not moved to another room (even though there was plenty available) so not great customer service. My advice to travellers would be to eat and drink outside the hotel as it is very pricey especially the main bar. It is a nice area and there are shops everywhere in Singapore so you do not have to worry about the location. Take a boat ride (about 5GBP per person). I stayed at the same chain of hotel in Kuala lumpur which I would recommend much more than this one, as the people were friendlier, the service better and the rooms much larger and the food was better value for money. Also sinagpore is very expensive compared to Malaysia (I would go as far to say it is more expensive then europe if not the same).

<Content>Another great stay at he Oriental in Singapore Just returned from another great stay (5 nights) at this hotel. Since the upgrade the hotel looks and feels so much better than before and the rooms are great with an excellent audio/video system. <Author>chalermchai
<Content>Rooms so comfortable you don't want to leave The Oriental Singapore has undergone major transformation and is now among the best appointed hotels in Asia. A local resident, I stayed one night over a long weekend and found the rooms so comfortable I didn't want to leave. Can't say the same for the FB options there though. Some highlights and lowlights:Highs:1) Rooms - Fabulously redecorated with smart layout, open concept baths, a very top class entertainment and technology system. I particularly like the choice of colours and fittings and full length windows. Very clean and streamlined look with carefully selected artpieces and a stylish feature-wall headboard. The bed was really comfortable with duvet, plump down pillows and good quality linen. Nice armchair and footrest. A very spacious working desk with real office chair and proper desk lamp, lots of storage space and counter topis to just spread out all your work documents or personal belongings, bathroom with a full-length window facing the bedroom area and the exterior view. Strategically placed mirrors including one in the bath to reflect the exterior view. The remote control is one of the best I've seen, designed to integrate all entertainment functions including the DVD player, radio, auxiliary audio and video systems and a touchscreen that actually lists all the channels available (which is a really good international selection). There is also an in-house radio channel named 'relax' which presents a really interesting compilation of chillout/spa/orient-inspired tunes. Rooms have iPod plug and play systems connected to Bose satellite speakers. In fact, you can also plug in gadgets such as x-boxes, etc. There is also a sub-woofer system. All powerpoints and cablepoints are at desk height, all powerpoints are universal so there's never a need for adaptors, all necessary cables are provided in a smart leather box and clearly marked with easy-to-understand instructions. Fruit platter and flowers come as standard. There seems to be a mid-day maid service (to replenish towels and touch-up bed) plus an evening turndown. Nothing much to fault really.2) Pool - Large area with secluded nooks and crannies and a nice view of the city skyline. Very attentive towel and drinks service. Poolside staff are very cheerful and enthusiastic.3) Views - I was given room 1230, an ocean view deluxe facing pockets of greenery and the sea dotted with ships and smaller vessels. The night I stayed there was a fireworks presentation as part of Singapore's national day celebrations. Very spectacular. I'l post some photos shortly.4) Front office - Very efficient and friendly. On check-in, the system was down but all paperwork was already printed out. The team handled guests to the best of their abilities. I requested for a late check-out with no problems. Check-out was just as quick and fuss-free.Lows:Only one significant low really:1) Breakfast - Had breakfast at Melt, the recently opened buffet restaurant. The spread was very big with interesting sections including Indian and a dessert area. But the actions of two staff members really made this a bad start to the day. The lady taking care of the juice counter has a permanent angry and frustrated face. She didn't seem interested in her work at all. When I helped myself to some mango yoghurt drink and swirled the jug to ensure the drink was properly mixed, she shouted very rudely: you don't need to shake that you know??? I corrected her by saying I was swirling and not shaking, and I didn't have to do it but wanted to do it. Her face exploded to an even ruder expression. I get even better service from the local hawker centres. Second staff was a male waiter who was trying very hard to explain to a Japanese couple the need to sign the breakfast bill even though breakfast is included in their room rate. He lost his temper and was really shouting at the couple:  just sign, it's only a statistic, the money will be deducted when you check out, CAN YOU JUST SIGN THIS BILL??? I really wonder, don't the restaurant staff undergo any form of training to deal with such simple situations? The same waiter, very shortly later, came to remove my plate while almost half of my toast was still on my hand and I was munching away. This is just not acceptable for a Mandarin Oriental property or any hospitality establishment for that matter.Verdict: I highly recommend this hotel. Probably the best rooms in the city right now, perhaps until the St Regis opens. Even Ritz-Carlton's rooms pale in comparison. Lots need to be addressed at the restaurant 'software' front. I'd rather walk to Marina Square nearby which has lots of more friendly and much cheaper food and dining options. Remember... bring your iPod! The sound quality is amazing...
